<h1 align=center style='text-align:center'><a name="_Toc62127923"></a><a

<h1 align=center style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-align:center'><a
name="_Toc62127924"></a><a name="_Toc62034875"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127924'><span

<h1><a name=general-context-and-history-of-diyabc></a><a name="_Toc62127927"><span
style='mso-bookmark:general-context-and-history-of-diyabc'><span lang=EN-US>1. (BRIEF)
INTRODUCTION</span></span></a></h1>

<h2><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127927'><span style='mso-bookmark:general-context-and-history-of-diyabc'><span
lang=EN-US>1.1 General context</span></span></span><span style='mso-bookmark:
general-context-and-history-of-diyabc'><span lang=EN-US> </span></span></h2>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>Simulation-based
methods such as Approximate Bayesian Computation (ABC) are well adapted to the
analysis of complex models of populations and species genetic history (Beaumont
2010). In this context, supervised machine learning (SML) methods provide
attractive statistical solutions to conduct efficient inferences about both
scenario choice and parameter estimation (</span><span class=SpellE><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Schrider</span></span><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> &amp; Kern 2018)</span><span
lang=EN-US>. The Random Forest methodology (RF) is a powerful ensemble of SML
algorithms used for both classification and/or regression problems (<span
class=SpellE>Breiman</span> 2001). RF allows conducting inferences at a lower
computational cost than ABC, without preliminary selection of the relevant
components of the ABC summary statistics, and bypassing the derivation of ABC
tolerance levels (<span class=SpellE>Pudlo</span> et al. 2018; <span
class=SpellE>Raynal</span> et al. 2019). We have implemented a set of RF
algorithms to process inferences using simulated datasets generated from an
extended version of the population genetic simulator implemented in DIYABC
v2.1.0 (<span class=SpellE>Cornuet</span> et al. 2014). The resulting computer
package, named DIYABC Random Forest v1.0, integrates two functionalities into a
user-friendly interface: the simulation under custom evolutionary scenarios of
different types of molecular data (microsatellites, DNA sequences or SNPs
&#8211; including traditional <span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'>IndSeq</b></span> and more recent <span class=SpellE><b
style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>PoolSeq</b></span> SNP data) and RF
treatments including statistical tools to evaluate the power and accuracy of
inferences (Collin et al. 2020). Because of the properties inherent of the
implemented RF methods and the large feature vector (including various summary
statistics and their linear combinations) available for SNP data, DIYABC Random
Forest v1.0 can efficiently contribute to the analysis of large-size SNP (and
other molecular markers) datasets to make inferences about complex population
genetic histories.<b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127928"><span lang=EN-US>1.2 How to cite the program DIYABC
Random Forest v1.0</span></a></h2>

<p class=MsoListParagraph style='margin-left:42.0pt;mso-add-space:auto'><span
lang=EN-US>Collin F-D, Durif G, <span class=SpellE>Raynal</span> L, <span
class=SpellE>Lombaert</span> E, Gautier M, Vitalis R, Marin J-M, Estoup A (2021)
DIYABC Random Forest v1.0: extending approximate Bayesian computation with
supervised machine learning to infer demographic history from genetic
polymorphisms. <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Molecular Ecology
Resources</i>. DOI: 10.22541/au.159480722.26357192</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127929"><span lang=EN-US>1.3 Web site</span></a></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US><a href="https://diyabc.github.io/"><span
class=InternetLink><span style='text-decoration:none;text-underline:none'>https://diyabc.github.io</span></span></a>.
</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>You can get from this <span
class=SpellE>github</span> site the executable files for different operating
systems, the latest version of this manual document, as well as examples of
DIYABC Random Forest analyses for different type of markers.</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127930"></a><a name=system-requirements><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127930'><span lang=EN-US>1.4. System requirement</span></span></a><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127930'><span lang=EN-US>s, installing and launching
the program</span></span></h2>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l17 level1 lfo39'><a
name=acknowledgements><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>The
software DIYABC Random Forest (hereafter DIYABC-RF) v1.0 is composed of three
parts: the dataset simulator, the Random Forest inference engine and the
graphical user interface. The whole is packaged as a standalone and
user-friendly graphical application named DIYABC-RF GUI and available at </span></a><a
href="https://diyabc.github.io/"><span style='mso-bookmark:acknowledgements'><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;color:windowtext;
text-decoration:none;text-underline:none'>https://diyabc.github.io</span></span></a><span
style='mso-bookmark:acknowledgements'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>.
The different developer and user manuals for each component of the software are
available on the same website. DIYABC-RF is a multithreaded software on three
operating systems: GNU/Linux, Microsoft Windows and MacOS. One can use the
program can be used through a modern and user-friendly graphical interface
designed as an R shiny application (Chang et al. 2019). For a fluid and
simplified user experience, this interface is available through a standalone
application, which does not </span></span><span style='mso-bookmark:acknowledgements'><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;mso-fareast-font-family:
Calibri'>require installing R or any dependencies </span></span><span
style='mso-bookmark:acknowledgements'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>and
hence can be used independently. The application is also implemented in an R
package providing a standard shiny web application (with the same graphical
interface) that can be run locally as any shiny application, or hosted as a web
service to provide a DIYABC-RF server for multiple users.</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l17 level1 lfo39'><span
style='mso-bookmark:acknowledgements'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>To
install and run the program, please check the instructions available on the
website https://diyabc.github.io/</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l17 level1 lfo39'><span
style='mso-bookmark:acknowledgements'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:

</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Minimum 4GB of RAM; 6GB of RAM
recommended</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l17 level1 lfo39'><span
style='mso-bookmark:acknowledgements'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:

</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>From 1 to 10 GB free disk space
for each </span></span><span style='mso-bookmark:acknowledgements'><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>DIYABC-RF</span><span
lang=EN-US> project depending on the project configuration and the number of
simulated datasets recorded in the training set file (<span class=SpellE>reftableRF.bin</span>
file).</span></span></p>

<h1><a name="_Toc62127932"><span lang=EN-US>2. FORMALIZATION OF SCENARIOS AND
GENERATION OF THE TRAINING SET</span></a></h1>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127933"></a><a name=basic-notions-on-abc></a><a
name=methodology></a><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127933'><span
style='mso-bookmark:basic-notions-on-abc'><span lang=EN-US>2.1 Basic notions</span></span></span></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>Before processing Random Forest
analyses, one need to generate a <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>training
set</i> which corresponds to the so called <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>reference
table</i> in a standard ABC framework (<span class=SpellE>Cornuet</span> et al.
2014 and see the associated program DIYABC v2.1.0). The datasets composing the
training set can be simulated under different models (hereafter referred to as
scenarios) and samples (i.e. <span class=SpellE>nb</span> of markers and
sampled individuals) configurations, using parameter values drawn from prior
distributions. Each resulting dataset is summarized using a set of descriptive
statistics. Scenarios and prior distributions are formalized in the main
pipeline of the software DIYABC Random Forest v1.0 (DIYABC-RF) and summary
statistics are computed using the &#8220;<u>Training set simulation</u>&#8221; module
of the main pipeline of DIYABC-RF, which essentially corresponds to an extended
version of the population genetics simulator implemented in DIYABC v2.1.0 (<span
class=SpellE>Cornuet</span> et al. 2014). As in the latter program, DIYABC-RF allows
considering complex population histories including any combination of
population divergence events, symmetrical or asymmetrical admixture events (but
not any continuous gene flow between populations) and changes in past
population size, with population samples potentially collected at different
times. Statistical analysis based on Random Forest algorithms of an observed
dataset using a given training set are computed using the &#8220;<u>Random
Forest Analysis&#8221;</u> module of the main pipeline of DIYABC-RF.</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127934"></a><a
name=X45f629f13f061e96ee74162059f3a93975759df><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127934'><span
lang=EN-US>2.2 Main features of algorithms for data simulation</span></span></a></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>The ABC part of DIYABC-RF is a simulation-based method. Data
simulation is based on the Wright-Fisher model. It consists in generating the
genealogy of all sampled genes until their most recent common ancestor using
(backward in time) coalescence theory. This begins by randomly drawing a
complete set of parameters from their own prior distributions and that satisfy
all imposed conditions. Then, once events have been ordered by increasing
times, a sequence of <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>actions</i> is
constructed. If there is more than one locus, the same sequence of actions is
used for all successive loci. </span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>Possible <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>actions</i> fall into
four categories:</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>- <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>adding a sample to a
population</b> = Add as many gene lineages to the population as there are genes
in the sample.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>- <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>merge two populations</b> =
Move the lineages of the second population into the first population.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>- <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>split between two
populations</b> = Distribute the lineages of the admixed population among the
two parental populations according to the admixture rate.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>- <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>coalesce and mutate
lineages within a population</b> = There are two possibilities here, depending
on whether the population is <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>terminal</i>
or not. We call <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>terminal</i> the
population including the most recent common ancestor of the whole genealogy. In
a terminal population, coalescences and mutations stop when the MRCA is reached
whereas in a non-terminal population, coalescence and mutations stop when the
upper (most ancient) limit is reached. In the latter case, coalescences can
stop before the upper limit is reached because there remains a single lineage,
but this single remaining lineage can still mutate. </span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:
36.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>Two different coalescence algorithms are implemented:
a generation by generation simulation or a continuous time simulation. The
choice, automatically performed by the program, is based on an empirical
criterion which ensures that the continuous time algorithm is chosen whenever
it is faster than generation by generation while keeping the relative error on
the coalescence rate below 5% (see <span class=SpellE>Cornuet</span> et al.
2008 for a description of this criterion). In any case, a coalescent tree is
generated over all sampled genes. </span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:
36.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>Then the mutational simulation process diverges
depending on the type of markers: for microsatellite or DNA sequence loci,
mutations are distributed over the branches according to a Poisson process
whereas for SNP loci, one mutation is applied to a single branch of the
coalescent tree, this branch being drawn at random with probability
proportional to its length. Eventually, starting from an ancestral allelic
state (established as explained below), all allelic states of the genealogy are
deduced forward in time according to the mutation process. For microsatellite
loci, the ancestral allelic state is taken at random in the stationary
distribution of the mutation model (not considering potential single nucleotide
indel mutations). For DNA sequence loci, the procedure is slightly more
complicated. First, the total number of mutations over the entire tree is
evaluated. Then according to the proportion of constant sites and the gamma
distribution of individual site mutation rates, the number and position of
mutated sites are generated. Finally, these mutated sites are given
&#8216;A&#8217;, &#8216;T&#8217;, &#8216;G&#8217; or &#8216;C&#8217; states
according to the selected mutation model. For SNP loci, the ancestral allelic state
is arbitrarily set to 0 and it becomes equal to 1 after mutation.</span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm style='text-indent:36.0pt'><span lang=EN-US
style='font-weight:normal'>Each category of loci has its own coalescence rate
deduced from male and female effective population sizes. In order to combine
different categories (e.g.&nbsp;autosomal and mitochondrial), we have to take
into account the relationships among the corresponding effective population
sizes. This can be achieved by linking the different effective population sizes
to the effective number of males ( </span><!--[if gte msEquation 12]><m:oMath><m:sSub><m:sSubPr><span

<h2><a name="_Toc62127935"></a><a name=historical-model-parameterization><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127935'><span lang=EN-US>2.3 Historical model
parameterization</span></span></a></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>The evolutionary scenario, which is
characterized by the historical model, can be described in a dedicated panel of
the interface of the program as a succession in time of &quot;events&quot; and
&quot;inter event periods&quot;. In the current version of the program, we
consider 4 categories of events: population divergence, discrete change of
effective population size, admixture and sampling (the last one <span
class=GramE>allow</span> considering samples taken at different times). Between
two successive events affecting a population, we assume that populations evolve
independently (e.g.&nbsp;without migration) and with a fixed effective size.
The usual parameters of the historical model are the times of occurrence of the
various events (counted in number of generations), the effective sizes of
populations and the admixture rates. <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>When
writing the scenario, events have to be coded sequentially backward in time</b>
(see section 2.3.2 for examples). Although this choice may not be natural at
first sight, it is coherent with coalescence theory on which are based all data
simulations in the program. For that reason, the keywords for a divergence or
an admixture event are </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>merge</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> and </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>split</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>, respectively. Two keywords </span><span class=SpellE><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>varNe</span></span></span><span lang=EN-US> and </span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>sample</span></span><span lang=EN-US> correspond to a discrete change
in effective population size and a gene sampling within a given population,
respectively. A scenario takes the form of a succession of lines (one line per
event), each line starting with the time of the event, then the nature of the
event, and ending with several other data depending on the nature of the event.
Following is the syntax used for each category of event:</span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR'>Population <span
class=SpellE>sample</span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

mso-fareast-language:FR;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape
 id="_x0000_i1025" type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:31.8pt;height:13.8pt'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image035.png"
  o:title="" chromakey="white"/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img width=42 height=18
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image036.gif" v:shapes="_x0000_i1025"><![endif]></span><![endif]><span
lang=EN-US>). Hereafter, only </span><!--[if gte msEquation 12]><m:oMath><i
 style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>&#10216;</m:r><m:r>pop</m:r><m:r>1</m:r><m:r>&#10217;</m:r></span></i></m:oMath><![endif]--><![if !msEquation]><span
style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:107%;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:"Times New Roman";
mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-fareast;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-bidi;
position:relative;top:2.5pt;mso-text-raise:-2.5pt;mso-ansi-language:FR;
mso-fareast-language:FR;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape
 id="_x0000_i1025" type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:34.8pt;height:13.8pt'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image029.png"
  o:title="" chromakey="white"/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img width=46 height=18
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image030.gif" v:shapes="_x0000_i1025"><![endif]></span><![endif]><span
lang=EN-US><span style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span>and </span><!--[if gte msEquation 12]><m:oMath><i
 style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>&#10216;</m:r><m:r>pop</m:r><m:r>2</m:r><m:r>&#10217;</m:r></span></i></m:oMath><![endif]--><![if !msEquation]><span
style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:107%;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:"Times New Roman";
mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-fareast;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-bidi;
position:relative;top:2.5pt;mso-text-raise:-2.5pt;mso-ansi-language:FR;
mso-fareast-language:FR;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape
 id="_x0000_i1025" type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:34.8pt;height:13.8pt'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image033.png"
  o:title="" chromakey="white"/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img width=46 height=18
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image034.gif" v:shapes="_x0000_i1025"><![endif]></span><![endif]><span
lang=EN-US><span style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span>&quot;remain&quot;.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>Note that one needs to write a first
line giving the <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>effective sizes of the
sampled populations before the first event described</b>, looking backward in
time. Expressions between arrows, other than population numbers, can be either
a numeric value (e.g.&nbsp;25) or a character string (e.g.&nbsp;</span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>t0</span></span><span lang=EN-US>). In the latter case, it is
considered as a parameter of the model. The program offers the possibility to
add or remove scenarios, by just clicking on the corresponding buttons. The
usual shortcuts (e.g. CTRL+C, CTRL+V and CTRL+X) can be used to edit the
different scenarios. Some or all parameters can be in common among scenarios.</span></p>

<h3 style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:10.0pt;margin-left:
0cm'><a name="_Toc62127936"><span lang=EN-US>2.3.1 Key notes</span></a></h3>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo3'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>1.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>There are two ways of giving a
fixed value to effective population sizes, times and admixture rates. Either
the fixed value appears as a numeric value in the scenario windows or it is
given as a string value like any parameter. In the latter case, one gives this
parameter a fixed value by choosing a Uniform distribution and setting the
minimum and maximum to that value in the prior setting of the corresponding
interface panel.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo3'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>2.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>All expressions must be
separated by at least one space.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo3'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>3.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>All expressions relative to
parameters can include sums or differences of parameters of the same type (e.g.
divergence times or effective population size but not a mixture of both). For
instance, it is possible to write:<br>
</span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;
mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>t0 merge 2 3</span></span><span lang=EN-US><br>
</span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;
mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>t0+t1 merge 1 2</span></span><span lang=EN-US><br>
This means that </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>t1</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> is the time elapsed between the two merge events. Note that one
cannot mix a parameter and a numeric value (e.g.&nbsp;</span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>t1+150</span></span><span lang=EN-US> will result in an error). This
can be done by writing </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>t1+t2</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> and fixing </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>t2</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> by choosing a uniform distribution with lower and upper bounds both
equal to 150 in the interface.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo3'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>4.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>Time is always given in generations</span></b><span lang=EN-US>.
Since we look backward, time increases towards past.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo3'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>5.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Negative times are allowed
(e.g.&nbsp;the example given in section 2.3.2), but not recommended.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo3'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>6.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Population numbers must be
consecutive natural integers starting at 1. The number of <span class=GramE>population</span>
can exceed the number of samples and vice versa: in other words, <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>unsampled populations</i> can be considered
in the scenario on one hand, and the same population can be sampled more than
once on the other hand.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo3'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>7.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>Multi-furcating population trees</span></b><span lang=EN-US> can be
considered, by writing <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>several
divergence events occurring at the same time.</b> However, one has to be
careful to the order of the </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>merge</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> events. For instance, the following piece of scenario will fail:<br>
</span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;
mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>100 merge 1 2</span></span><span lang=EN-US><br>
</span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;
mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>100 merge 2 3</span></span><span lang=EN-US><br>
This is because, after the first line, population 2, which has merged with
population 1, does not &quot;exist&quot; anymore (the remaining population is
population 1). So, it cannot receive lineages of population 3 as it should as a
result of the second line. The correct ways are either to put line 2 before
line 1, or to change line 2 to:<br>
</span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;
mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>100 merge 1 3</span></span><span lang=EN-US>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo3'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>8.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Since times of events can be
parameters, the order of events can change according to the values taken by the
time parameters. In any case, before simulating a dataset, the program sorts
out events by increasing times. Note that sorting out events by increasing times
can only be done when all time values are known, i.e.&nbsp;when simulating
datasets. When checking scenarios in the interface, all time values are not yet
defined, so that when visualizing a scenario, events are represented in the
same order as they appear in the window used to define the scenario. If two or
more events occur at the same time, the order is that of the scenario as it is
written by the user.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo3'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>9.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Most scenarios begin with
sampling events. We then need to know the effective size of the populations to
perform the simulation of coalescences until the next event concerning each
population. We decided to provide the effective size (first line) and the
sampling description (following lines) on distinct lines.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-pagination:
widow-orphan lines-together;page-break-after:avoid;mso-outline-level:3'><a
name="_Toc62127937"><b><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:major-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'>2.3.2 Examples</span></b></a><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:major-latin;
mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:major-fareast;
mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;color:#4F81BD;
mso-themecolor:accent1'><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>Below are some usual scenarios with
increasing complexity. Each scenario is coded (as in the corresponding
interface panel of the program) on the left side and a graphic representation
(given by DIYABC Random Forest) is printed on the right side</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l31 level1 lfo4'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>1.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>One population from which
several samples have been taken at various generations: 0, 3 and 10. Generation
0 could correspond for instance to the most recent sampling date. The only
unknown historical-demographical parameter of the scenario is the (constant)
effective population size which is defined in the first line at sampling time.<br
style='mso-special-character:line-break'>
<![if !supportLineBreakNewLine]><br style='mso-special-character:line-break'>
<![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l31 level1 lfo4'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>2.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Two populations of size </span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>N1</span></span><span lang=EN-US> and </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>N2</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> (defined in the first line at sampling time) have diverged </span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>t</span></span><span lang=EN-US> generations in the past from an
ancestral population of size </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>N1+N2</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>.<br style='mso-special-character:line-break'>
<![if !supportLineBreakNewLine]><br style='mso-special-character:line-break'>
<![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l31 level1 lfo4'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>3.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Two parental populations (1 and
1) with constant effective population sizes </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>N1</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> and </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>N2</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> have diverged at time </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>td</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> from an ancestral population of size </span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>NA</span></span><span lang=EN-US>. At time </span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>ta</span></span><span lang=EN-US>, there has been an <u>admixture event</u>
between the two populations giving birth to an admixed population (3) with
effective size </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>N3</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> and with an admixture rate </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>ra</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> relative to population 1.<br style='mso-special-character:line-break'>
<![if !supportLineBreakNewLine]><br style='mso-special-character:line-break'>
<![endif]></span></p>

 mso-padding-alt:0cm 5.4pt 0cm 5.4pt'>
 <tr style='mso-yfti-irow:0;mso-yfti-firstrow:yes;mso-yfti-lastrow:yes'>
  <td width=192 valign=top style='width:144.3pt;padding:0cm 5.4pt 0cm 5.4pt'>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l31 level1 lfo4'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>4.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The next scenario includes <u>four
population samples and two admixture events</u>. All populations have identical
effective sizes (</span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>Ne</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>).<br style='mso-special-character:line-break'>
<![if !supportLineBreakNewLine]><br style='mso-special-character:line-break'>
<![endif]></span></p>

<table class=Table border=0 cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 width=561

  <p class=Compact align=center style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-align:center;

  lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;
  mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'><span

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l8 level1 lfo1'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Note that although there are
only four samples, the scenario includes a fifth <u>unsampled population</u>.
This unsampled population which diverged from population 1 at time </span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>t3</span></span><span lang=EN-US> was a parent in the admixture event
occurring at time </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>t2</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>. Note also that the first line must include the effective sizes of
the <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>five</i> populations.</span></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst style='margin-left:24.0pt;mso-add-space:
auto;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l31 level1 lfo4'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>5.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Example of DIYABC-RF code for <u>unidirectional
admixture/introgression</u> where a fraction r2 of genes from population 'Pop
2' (with an effective population size N2) <span class=SpellE>introgresses</span>
into population 'Pop 1' (with a population size N1) at time t1. The code also
describes the merge of the two populations 'Pop 1' and 'Pop 2' into a common
ancestor (with a population size Na) at time t2. It is worth noting that: (<span
class=SpellE>i</span>) in the observed datafile, there are only two sampled
populations (Pop 1 and Pop 2) and the user will need to define two (additional)
<u>unsampled</u> populations in the first line of code (Pop 3 and Pop 4); (ii) we
advise in this case to draw the fraction of genes transferred during the unidirectional
admixture (r2) into a uniform distribution with min and max bounds equal to <span
class=SpellE>eg.</span> 0.01 (very weak introgression from 'Pop 2' into 'Pop
1') and 0.5 (strong introgression from 'Pop 2' into 'Pop 1'), respectively.</span></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle style='margin-left:24.0pt;mso-add-space:
auto'><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle style='margin-left:24.0pt;mso-add-space:
auto'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_24" o:spid="_x0000_s1026"

</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img width=301 height=272
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image054.jpg" align=left
hspace=12 v:shapes="Image_x0020_24"><![endif]><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:

style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></b><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:
"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'># comment 1</span></i><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:

FR'><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle style='margin-left:24.0pt;mso-add-space:
auto'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'>0 <span class=SpellE>sample</span>
1<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle style='margin-left:24.0pt;mso-add-space:
auto'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;

2<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle style='margin-left:24.0pt;mso-add-space:
auto'><span class=GramE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'>t</span></b></span><b
style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:

1'> </span></b></span></i><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'><span
style='mso-tab-count:2'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle style='margin-left:24.0pt;mso-add-space:
auto'><span class=GramE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'>t</span></b></span><b
style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:
"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'>1 merge 1 3<span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp; </span><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span></span></b><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:

FR'># comment 3</span></i><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle style='margin-left:24.0pt;mso-add-space:
auto'><span class=GramE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'>t</span></b></span><b
style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:
"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'>2 merge 1 4<span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span></span></b><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:
normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:
FR'># comment 4</span></i><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpLast style='margin-left:24.0pt;mso-add-space:auto'><span
class=GramE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'>t</span></b></span><b
style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:
"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'>2 VarNe 1 Na<span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span></span></b><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:
normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:
FR'># comment 5</span></i><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
style='font-size:10.0pt;font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;
mso-ansi-language:FR'><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:9.0pt'># comment 1: both unsampled populations 'Pop
3' and 'Pop 4' correspond to 'Pop 2', hence their population sizes N2.</span><span
lang=EN-US><br>
</span></i><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:9.0pt'># comment 2: at time t1 a fraction r2 of genes from
'Pop 2' goes into the unsampled population 'Pop 3' and a fraction 1-r2 goes
into the unsampled population 'Pop 4' ('Pop 2' disappears)<o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:9.0pt'># comment 3: we immediately merge (cf. still
time t1) the unsampled population 'Pop 3' (with the fraction r2 of genes from
'Pop 2') into the population 'Pop 1' - hence the unidirectional admixture of r2
genes from 'Pop 2' into 'Pop 1' ('Pop 3' disappears)<o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:9.0pt'># comment 4: 'Pop 4' - which now corresponds
to the ex-'Pop 2' with the fraction 1-r2 of genes - can be merge into 'Pop 1'<o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraph style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:
0cm;margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-add-space:auto'><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:9.0pt'>#
comment 5: the population ancestral to 'Pop 1' and 'Pop 2' now has its own
population size Na<o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt'><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l31 level1 lfo4'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>6.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The following three scenarios
correspond to a classic invasion history from an ancestral population
(population 1<u>). In scenario 1, population 3 is derived from population 2,
itself derived from population 1. In scenario 2, population 2 derived from
population 3, itself derived from population 1. In scenario 3, both populations
2 and 3 derived independently from population 1.</u> Note that when a new
population is created from its ancestral population, there is an initial size
reduction (noted here </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>N2b</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> for population 2 and </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>N3b</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> for population 3) for a given number of generation (here </span><span
class=SpellE><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:Consolas;mso-bidi-font-family:
Consolas'>db</span></span><span lang=EN-US> for both populations) mimicking a
demographic bottleneck since the invasive population generally starts with a
few immigrants. For instance, a low number of <span class=SpellE>Nxb</span>
individuals for <span class=SpellE>db</span> generations could corresponds to <span
class=SpellE>Nxb</span> values ranging between 5 to 100 individuals and <span
class=SpellE>db</span> values ranging from 1 to 10 generations (e.g. <span
class=SpellE>Fraimout</span> et al. 2017). If <span class=SpellE>db</span> = 0
then no bottleneck occurs which can be also a coding choice.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US><span style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;
</span>Scenario 1</span></p>

<table class=Table border=0 cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 width=601
 style='width:450.6pt;border-collapse:collapse;mso-yfti-tbllook:1984;
 mso-padding-alt:0cm 5.4pt 0cm 5.4pt'>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127938"></a><a
name=Xc43f7bb58de29b50adf97c1b0251e0ff311883c><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127938'><span
lang=EN-US>2.4 Mutation model parameterization (microsatellite and DNA sequence
loci)</span></span></a></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>The program can analyze microsatellite
data and DNA sequence data altogether as well as separately. SNP loci can be
also analyzed separately from microsatellite data and DNA sequence data. It is
worth stressing that all loci in an analysis must be <u>genetically independent</u>.
Second, for DNA sequence loci, <span class=SpellE>intralocus</span>
recombination is not considered. Loci are grouped by the user according to its
needs. For microsatellite and DNA sequence, a different mutation model can be
defined for each group. For instance, one group can include all microsatellites
with motifs that are 2 bp long and another group those with a 4 bp long motif.
Also, with DNA sequence loci, nuclear loci can be grouped together and a
mitochondrial locus form a separate group. <u>SNPs do not require mutation
model parameterization (see below for details)</u>.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>We now describe the parameterization
of microsatellite and DNA sequence markers.</span></p>

<h3><a name="_Toc62127939"></a><a name=microsatellite-loci><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127939'><span lang=EN-US>2.4.1 Microsatellite loci</span></span></a></h3>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>Although a variety of mutation models have been proposed for
microsatellite loci, it is usually sufficient to consider only the simplest
models (e.g. Estoup et al. 2002). This has the non-negligible advantage of
reducing the number of parameters. This is why we chose the Generalized
Stepwise Mutation model (GSM). Under this model, a mutation increases or
decreases the length of the microsatellite by a number of repeated motifs
following a geometric distribution. This model necessitates only two
parameters: the mutation rate (</span><span class=VerbatimChar><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>&micro;</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>) and the parameter of the geometric distribution (</span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>P</span></span><span lang=EN-US>). The same mutation model is imposed
to all loci of a given group. However, each locus has its own parameters
(&micro;<span class=SpellE><sub>i</sub></span> and P<sub>i</sub></span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>) </span></span><span lang=EN-US>and, following a hierarchical scheme,
each locus parameter is drawn from a gamma distribution with mean equal to the
mean parameter value. </span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>Note also that:</span></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpFirst style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;
margin-bottom:0cm;margin-left:54.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-add-space:auto;
text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l19 level1 lfo13'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>1.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Individual loci parameters
(&micro;<span class=SpellE>i</span> and Pi) are considered as nuisance
parameters and hence are never recorded. Only mean parameters are recorded.</span></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;
margin-bottom:0cm;margin-left:54.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-add-space:auto;
text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l19 level1 lfo13'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>2.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The variance or shape parameter
of the gamma distributions are set by the user and are NOT considered as
parameters.</span></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpMiddle style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;
margin-bottom:0cm;margin-left:54.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-add-space:auto;
text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l19 level1 lfo13'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>3.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The SMM or Stepwise Mutation
Model is a special case of the GSM in which the number of repeats involved in a
mutation is always one. Such a model can be easily achieved by setting the
maximum value of mean P (</span><!--[if gte msEquation 12]><m:oMath><m:bar><m:barPr><m:pos
    m:val="top"/><span style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif;mso-ascii-font-family:
   "Cambria Math";mso-hansi-font-family:"Cambria Math"'><m:ctrlPr></m:ctrlPr></span></m:barPr><m:e><i
   style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>P</m:r></span></i></m:e></m:bar></m:oMath><![endif]--><![if !msEquation]><span
style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:107%;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:"Times New Roman";
mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-fareast;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-bidi;
position:relative;top:2.5pt;mso-text-raise:-2.5pt;mso-ansi-language:FR;
mso-fareast-language:FR;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape
 id="_x0000_i1025" type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:7.8pt;height:16.2pt'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image067.png"
  o:title="" chromakey="white"/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img width=10 height=22
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image068.gif" v:shapes="_x0000_i1025"><![endif]></span><![endif]><span
lang=EN-US>) to 0. In this case, all loci have their </span><!--[if gte msEquation 12]><m:oMath><m:sSub><m:sSubPr><span
   style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif;mso-ascii-font-family:"Cambria Math";
   mso-hansi-font-family:"Cambria Math"'><m:ctrlPr></m:ctrlPr></span></m:sSubPr><m:e><i
   style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>P</m:r></span></i></m:e><m:sub><i
   style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>i</m:r></span></i></m:sub></m:sSub></m:oMath><![endif]--><![if !msEquation]><span
style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:107%;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:"Times New Roman";
mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-fareast;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-bidi;
position:relative;top:2.5pt;mso-text-raise:-2.5pt;mso-ansi-language:FR;
mso-fareast-language:FR;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape
 id="_x0000_i1025" type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:10.2pt;height:13.8pt'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image069.png"
  o:title="" chromakey="white"/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img width=14 height=18
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image070.gif" v:shapes="_x0000_i1025"><![endif]></span><![endif]><span
lang=EN-US><span style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span>set equal to 0 whatever
the shape of the gamma distribution.</span></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraphCxSpLast style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;
margin-bottom:0cm;margin-left:54.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-add-space:auto;
text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l19 level1 lfo13'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>4.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>All loci can be given the same
value of a parameter by setting the shape of the corresponding gamma
distribution to 0 (this is NOT a limiting case of the gamma, but only a way of
telling the program).</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>To give more flexibility to the mutation model, the program offers
the possibility to consider <u>mutations that insert or delete a single
nucleotide</u> to the microsatellite sequence by using a mean parameter (named </span><!--[if gte msEquation 12]><m:oMath><m:sSub><m:sSubPr><span
   style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif;mso-ascii-font-family:"Cambria Math";
   mso-hansi-font-family:"Cambria Math"'><m:ctrlPr></m:ctrlPr></span></m:sSubPr><m:e><i
   style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>&#956;</m:r></span></i></m:e><m:sub><m:d><m:dPr><span
     style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif;mso-ascii-font-family:"Cambria Math";
     mso-hansi-font-family:"Cambria Math"'><m:ctrlPr></m:ctrlPr></span></m:dPr><m:e><i
     style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
     "Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>SNI</m:r></span></i></m:e></m:d></m:sub></m:sSub></m:oMath><![endif]--><![if !msEquation]><span
style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:107%;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:"Times New Roman";
mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-fareast;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-bidi;
position:relative;top:4.5pt;mso-text-raise:-4.5pt;mso-ansi-language:FR;
mso-fareast-language:FR;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape
 id="_x0000_i1025" type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:28.8pt;height:24.6pt'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image071.png"
  o:title="" chromakey="white"/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img width=38 height=33
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image072.gif" v:shapes="_x0000_i1025"><![endif]></span><![endif]><span
lang=EN-US>) with a prior to be defined and individual loci having either
values identical to the mean parameter or drawn from a Gamma distribution.</span></p>

<h3><a name="_Toc62127940"></a><a name=dna-sequence-loci><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127940'><span lang=EN-US>2.4.2 DNA sequence loci</span></span></a></h3>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>The program does not consider
insertion-deletion mutations, mainly because there does not seem to be much
consensus on this topic. Concerning substitutions, only the simplest models are
considered. We chose the Jukes-Cantor (1969) one parameter model, the Kimura
(1980) two parameter model, the Hasegawa-<span class=SpellE>Kishino</span>-Yano
(1985) and the Tamura-<span class=SpellE>Nei</span> (1993) models. The last two
models include the ratios of each nucleotide as parameters. In order to reduce
the number of parameters, these ratios have been fixed to the values calculated
from the observed dataset for each DNA sequence locus. Consequently, this
leaves two and three parameters for the Hasegawa-<span class=SpellE>Kishino</span>-Yano
(HKY) and Tamura-<span class=SpellE>Nei</span> (TN), respectively. Also, two
adjustments are possible: one can fix the fraction of constant sites (those
that cannot mutate) on the one hand and the shape of the Gamma distribution of
mutations among sites on the other hand. As for microsatellites, all sequence
loci of the same group are given the same mutation model with mean parameter(s)
drawn from priors and each locus has its own parameter(s) drawn from a Gamma
distribution (same hierarchical scheme). Notes 1, 2 and 4 of previous
subsection (2.4.1) apply also for sequence loci.</span></p>

<h3><a name="_Toc62127941"></a><a
name=X967a0daa6c052f45bf185add8c047b9aac1fd89><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127941'><span
lang=EN-US>2.4.3 SNPs do not require mutation model parameterization</span></span></a><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127941'><span lang=EN-US> &#8211; notion of MAF and
MRC</span></span></h3>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>SNPs have two characteristics that
allow to get rid of mutation models: they are (necessarily) polymorphic and
they present only two allelic states (ancestral and derived). In order to be
sure that all analyzed SNP loci have the two characteristics, <u>non-polymorphic
loci are discarded right from the beginning of analyses</u>. Note that a
warning message will appear if the observed dataset include monomorphic loci,
the latter being automatically removed from further analyses by the program.
Consequently, one can assume that there occurred one and only one mutation in
the coalescence tree of sampled genes. We will see below that this largely
simplifies (and speeds up) SNP data simulation as one can use in this case the
efficient &#8220;-s&#8221; algorithm of Hudson (2002) (<span class=SpellE>Cornuet</span>
et al.&nbsp;2014). Also, this advantageously reduces the dimension of the
parameter space as mutation parameters are not needed in this case. There is
however a potential drawback which is the absence of any calibration generally
brought by priors on mutation parameters. <u>Consequently, time/effective size
ratios rather than original time or effective size parameters will be
informative</u>.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='text-indent:36.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>It is worth
noting that, using the Hudson&#8217;s simulation algorithm for SNP markers
leads to applying a default <u>MAF (minimum allele frequency)</u> criterion on
the simulated dataset. As a matter of fact, each locus in both the observed and
simulated datasets will be characterized by the presence of at least one copy
of the SNP alleles over all genes sampled from all studied populations (i.e.
pooling all genes genotyped at the locus). In DIYABC Random Forest v1.0, it is
possible to impose a given MAF criterion on the observed and simulated
datasets. This MAF is computed pooling all genes genotyped over all studied
population samples. For instance, the specification of a MAF equal to 5% will
automatically select a subset of <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>m</i>
loci characterized by a minimum allele frequency &gt; 5% out of the <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>l</i> loci of the observed dataset. In
agreement with this, only <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>m</i> loci with
a MAF&gt;5% will be retained in a simulated dataset. </span><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:CMR10'>In practice, the instruction for a given MAF
has to be indicated directly in the headline of the file of the observed
dataset (see section 7.1.1 for data file examples). For instance, if one wants
to consider only loci with a MAF equal to 5% one will write </span><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:CMMI10'>&lt;</span><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:CMSS10'>MAF=0.05</span><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:CMMI10'>&gt; </span><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:CMR10'>in the headline. Writing </span><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:CMMI10'>&lt;</span><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:CMSS10'>MAF=<span class=SpellE>hudson</span></span><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:CMMI10'>&gt; </span><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:CMR10'>(or omitting to write any instruction with
respect to the MAF) will bring the program to use the standard Hudson's
algorithm without further selection. The selection of a subset of loci fitting
a given MAF allows: (<span class=SpellE>i</span>) to remove the loci with very
low level of polymorphism from the dataset and hence increase the mean level of
genetic variation of both the observed and simulated datasets, without producing
any bias in the analyses; and (ii) to reduce the proportion of loci for which
the observed variation may corresponds to sequencing errors.</span><span
lang=EN-US> In practice MAF values &#8804;10% are considered. To check for the
consistency/robustness of the ABC results obtained, it may be useful to treat a
SNP dataset considering different MAFs (for instance MAF=<span class=SpellE>hudson</span>,
MAF=1% and MAF=5%).</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='text-indent:36.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>It is worth
stressing that the MAF criterion applies to standard Individual sequencing
(hereafter <span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>IndSeq</b></span>)
SNP data.<span style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp; </span>In addition to <span
class=SpellE>IndSeq</span> data, DIYABC Random Forest v1.0 allows the
simulation and analyses of pool-sequencing SNP data (hereafter <span
class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>PoolSeq</b></span> data),
which basically consist of whole-genome sequences of pools of tens to hundreds
of individual DNAs (Gautier et al., 2013; <span class=SpellE>Schl&ouml;tterer</span>
et al., 2014). In practice, the simulation of <span class=SpellE>PoolSeq</span>
data consists first in simulating individual SNP genotypes for all individuals
in each population pool, and then generating pool read counts from a binomial
distribution parameterized with the simulated allele counts (obtained from
individual SNP genotypes) and the total pool read coverage (e.g., <span
class=SpellE>Hivert</span>, et al. 2018). A criterion somewhat similar to the
MAF was implemented for <span class=SpellE>PoolSeq</span> data: <u>the minimum
read count (MRC)</u>. The MRC is the number of sequence reads of the minor
allele frequency allele when pooling the reads <span class=SpellE>over all</span>
population samples. The specification of a MRC equal for instance to 5 will
automatically select a subset of <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>m</i> <span
class=SpellE>PoolSeq</span> loci characterized by more than five reads over all
studied pools among the <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>l</i> loci of the
observed dataset. In agreement with this, only <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:
normal'>m</i> loci with more than five reads will be retained in a simulated
dataset.</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127942"></a><a name=prior-distributions><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127942'><span lang=EN-US>2.5 Prior distributions</span></span></a></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>The Bayesian aspect of the ABC-RF
approach implies that parameter estimations use prior knowledge about these
parameters that is given by prior distributions of parameters. The program
offers a choice among usual probability distributions, i.e.&nbsp;Uniform,
Log-Uniform, Normal or Log-Normal for historical parameters and Uniform,
Log-Uniform or Gamma for mutation parameters. Extremum values (min and max) and
other parameters (e. g. mean and standard deviation) must be filled in by the
user. It is worth noting that one can impose some simple conditions on
historical parameters. For instance, there can be two times parameters with
overlapping prior distributions. However, we want that the first one, say </span><span
class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt'>t1</span></span><span lang=EN-US>, to always be larger than the second
one, say </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:
11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>t2</span></span><span lang=EN-US>. For that,
we just need to set </span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>t1</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>&gt;</span><span class=VerbatimChar><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt'>t2</span></span><span
lang=EN-US> in the corresponding edit-windows. Such a condition needs to be
between two parameters and more precisely between two parameters of the same
category (i.e.&nbsp;two effective sizes, two times or two admixture rates). The
limit to the number of conditions is imposed by the logics, not by the program.
The only binary relationships accepted here are &lt;, &gt;, &#8804;, and
&#8805;.</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127943"></a><a name=summary-statistics><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127943'><span lang=EN-US>2.6 Summary statistics</span></span></a><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127943'><span lang=EN-US> as components of the
feature vector</span></span><span lang=EN-US> </span></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>The training set includes values of a feature vector which is a
multidimensional representation of any data point (i.e. simulated or observed
datasets) made up of measurements (or features) taken from it. More
specifically, the feature vector includes a large number of statistics that
summarize genetic variation in the way that they allow capturing different
aspects of gene genealogies and hence various features of molecular patterns
generated by selectively neutral population histories (e.g. Beaumont 2010; <span
class=SpellE>Cornuet</span> et al. 2014). For each category (microsatellite,
DNA sequences or SNP) of loci, the program proposes a series of summary
statistics among those used by population geneticists. </span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span lang=EN-US>Note: The code name of each statistic
mentioned in the various program outputs is given between brackets [XXX] in
sections 2.6.1, 2.6.2 and 2.6.3.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<h3 style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:10.0pt;margin-left:
0cm'><a name="_Toc62127944"></a><a name=for-microsatellite-loci><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127944'><span lang=EN-US>2.6.1 For microsatellite
loci</span></span></a></h3>

<p class=DefinitionTerm><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm><span lang=EN-US>Single sample statistics:</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l24 level1 lfo5'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>1.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[NAL] - mean number of alleles
across loci</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l24 level1 lfo5'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>2.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>[HET] - mean gene
diversity across loci (<span class=SpellE>Nei</span> 1987)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.1pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-24.1pt;mso-list:l24 level1 lfo5'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>3.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>[VAR] - mean allele
size variance across loci</span></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraph style='margin-left:24.0pt;mso-add-space:auto;
text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l24 level1 lfo5'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>4.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>[MGW] - mean M index
across loci (Garza and Williamson 2001; <span class=SpellE>Excoffier</span> et
al. 2005)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-bottom:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm><span lang=EN-US>Two sample statistics:</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l3 level1 lfo6'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>1.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[N2P] - mean number of alleles
across loci (two samples)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l3 level1 lfo6'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>2.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[H2P] - mean gene diversity
across loci (two samples)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l3 level1 lfo6'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>3.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[V2P] - mean allele size
variance across loci (two samples)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l3 level1 lfo6'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>4.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US style='mso-fareast-font-family:
Cambria;mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-fareast'><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>[FST] -</span><!--[if gte msEquation 12]><m:oMath><m:sSub><m:sSubPr><span

   style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>ST</m:r></span></i></m:sub></m:sSub></m:oMath><![endif]--><![if !msEquation]><span

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l3 level1 lfo6'><![if !supportLists]><span

</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>[LIK] - mean index of
classification (two samples) </span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span><span style='mso-ansi-language:
FR'>(<span class=SpellE>Rannala</span> and <span class=SpellE>Moutain</span> <span
class=GramE>1997;</span> Pascual et al. 2007)<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l3 level1 lfo6'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
