</span></span></span><![endif]><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR'><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>[DAS] - shared allele distance between two samples (Chakraborty and <span
class=SpellE>Jin</span> 1993)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l3 level1 lfo6'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>7.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US style='mso-fareast-font-family:
Cambria;mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-fareast'><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>[DM2] -<span style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp; </span>distance between
two samples (<span class=SpellE>Golstein</span> et al. 1995)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-bottom:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm><span lang=EN-US>Three sample statistics:</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l30 level1 lfo7'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>1.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[AML] - Maximum likelihood
coefficient of admixture (<span class=SpellE>Choisy</span> et al. 2004)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-bottom:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<h3 style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:10.0pt;margin-left:
0cm'><a name="_Toc62127945"></a><a name=for-dna-sequence-loci><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127945'><span lang=EN-US>2.6.2 For DNA sequence loci</span></span></a></h3>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm><span lang=EN-US>Single sample statistics:</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l33 level1 lfo8'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>1.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[NHA] - number of distinct
haplotypes</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l33 level1 lfo8'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>2.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[NSS] - number of segregating
sites</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l33 level1 lfo8'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>3.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[MPD] - mean pairwise
difference</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l33 level1 lfo8'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>4.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[VPD] - variance of the number
of pairwise differences</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l33 level1 lfo8'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>5.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>[DTA] - Tajima&#8217;s
D statistics (Tajima 1989)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l33 level1 lfo8'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>6.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[PSS] - Number of private
segregating sites </span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-bottom:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:
36.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>(=number of segregating sites if there is only one
sample)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l33 level1 lfo8'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>7.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[MNS] - Mean of the numbers of
the rarest nucleotide at segregating sites</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l33 level1 lfo8'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>8.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[VNS] - Variance of the numbers
of the rarest nucleotide at segregating sites</span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm><span lang=EN-US>Two sample statistics:</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l38 level1 lfo9'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>1.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[NH2] - number of distinct
haplotypes in the pooled sample</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l38 level1 lfo9'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>2.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[NS2] - number of segregating
sites in the pooled sample</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l38 level1 lfo9'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>3.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[MP2] - mean of within sample
pairwise differences</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:0cm;
mso-list:l38 level1 lfo9'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>4.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[MPB] - mean of between sample
pairwise differences</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l38 level1 lfo9'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>5.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US style='mso-fareast-font-family:
Cambria;mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-fareast'><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>[HST] -</span><!--[if gte msEquation 12]><m:oMath><m:sSub><m:sSubPr><span
   style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif;mso-ascii-font-family:"Cambria Math";
   mso-hansi-font-family:"Cambria Math"'><m:ctrlPr></m:ctrlPr></span></m:sSubPr><m:e><i
   style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>F</m:r></span></i></m:e><m:sub><i
   style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>ST</m:r></span></i></m:sub></m:sSub></m:oMath><![endif]--><![if !msEquation]><span
style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:107%;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:"Times New Roman";
mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-fareast;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-bidi;
position:relative;top:2.5pt;mso-text-raise:-2.5pt;mso-ansi-language:FR;
mso-fareast-language:FR;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape
 id="_x0000_i1025" type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:16.2pt;height:13.8pt'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image073.png"
  o:title="" chromakey="white"/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img width=22 height=18
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image074.gif" v:shapes="_x0000_i1025"><![endif]></span><![endif]><span
lang=EN-US><span style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span>between two samples
(Hudson et al. 1992)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-bottom:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm style='margin-left:2.85pt'><span lang=EN-US>Three
sample statistics:</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:24.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l9 level1 lfo10'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>1.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>[SML] Maximum likelihood
coefficient of admixture (adapted from <span class=SpellE>Choisy</span> et al.
2004)</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-bottom:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<h3 style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:10.0pt;margin-left:
2.85pt'><a name="_Toc62127946"></a><a name=for-snp-loci><span style='mso-bookmark:
_Toc62127946'><span lang=EN-US>2.6.3 For SNP loci</span></span></a></h3>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US>In addition to
&#8220;standard&#8221; individual-sequencing SNP data (i.e. <span class=SpellE><b
style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>IndSeq</b></span> data), the program allows
the simulation and analyses of pool-sequencing SNP data (i.e. <span
class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>PoolSeq</b></span> data),
which basically consist of whole-genome sequences of pools of tens to hundreds
of individual DNAs (Gautier et al., 2013; <span class=SpellE>Schl&ouml;tterer</span>
et al., 2014). For both <span class=SpellE>IndSeq</span> and <span
class=SpellE>PoolSeq</span> SNPs, we have implemented the following (same) set
of summary statistics. </span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US>1. <span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[ML1p]
[ML2p] [ML3p] [ML4p] - <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Proportion of
monomorphic loci</i> for each population, as well as for each pair, triplet and
quadruplet of populations. </span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>Mean (m suffix added to the code name) and variance (v suffix) over
loci values are computed for all subsequent summary statistics<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US>2. <span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[<span
class=SpellE>HWm</span>] [<span class=SpellE>HWv</span>] [<span class=SpellE>HBm</span>]
[<span class=SpellE>HBv</span>] - <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Heterozygosity</i>
for each population and for each pair of populations (<span class=SpellE>Hivert</span>
et al. 2018). </span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US>3.<span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[FST1m]
[FST1v] [FST2m] [FST2v] [FST3m] [FST3v] [FST4m] [FST4v] [<span class=SpellE>FSTGm</span>]
[<span class=SpellE>FSTGv</span>] - <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>FST</i>-<i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>related statistics</i> for each population
(i.e., population-specific FST; Weir &amp; <span class=SpellE>Goudet</span>
2017), for each pair, triplet, quadruplet and overall populations (when the
dataset includes more than four populations) (<span class=SpellE>Hivert</span>
et al. 2018). </span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US>4. <span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[F3m]
[F3v] [F4m] [F4v] - <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Patterson&#8217;s
f-statistics</i> for each triplet (f3-statistics) and quadruplet
(f4-statistics) of populations (Patterson et al. 2012 and <span class=SpellE>Leblois</span>
et al. 2018 for the <span class=SpellE>PoolSeq</span> unbiased f3-statistics) </span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US>5. <span
style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[<span
class=SpellE>NEIm</span>] [<span class=SpellE>NEIv</span>] - <span
class=SpellE><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Nei&#8217;s</i></span><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'> (1972) distance</i> for each pair of
populations</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US>6. <span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[<span
class=SpellE>AMLm</span>] [<span class=SpellE>AMLv</span>] - <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Maximum likelihood coefficient of admixture</i>
computed for each triplet of populations (adapted from <span class=SpellE>Choisy</span>
et al. 2004).</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127947"><span lang=EN-US>2.7 Generating the training set</span></a></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span
lang=EN-US>The training set can include as many scenarios as desired. The prior
probability of each scenario is uniform so that each scenario will have
approximately the same number of simulated datasets. Only parameters that are
defined for the drawn scenario are generated from their respective prior
distribution. Scenarios may or may not share parameters. When conditions apply
to some parameters (see section 2.3), parameter sets are drawn in their
respective prior distributions until all conditions are fulfilled. The simulated
datasets (summarized with the statistics detailed in section 2.6) of the
training set are recorded for further statistical analyses (using Random Forest
algorithms) in a key binary file named <span class=SpellE><u>reftableRF.bin</u></span>.
</span><a name=the-graphic-user-interface><b><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:
16.0pt;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:major-latin;
mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:major-fareast;
mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;color:#4F81BD;
mso-themecolor:accent1'><o:p></o:p></span></b></a></p>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span lang=EN-US>3. <a
name="_Toc62127948">RANDOM FOREST ANALYSIS</a></span></span></h1>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Cambria",serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;color:black;mso-themecolor:text1;font-weight:
normal;mso-bidi-font-weight:bold'>Once the training set has been generated, one
can start various statistical treatments using the Random Forest (RF)
algorithms implemented in the program and by running the &#8220;Random Forest
analyses&#8221; module</span></span></h1>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a name="_Toc62127950"><span
lang=EN-US>3.1 Addition of linear combinations of summary statistics to the vector
feature</span></a><span lang=EN-US> </span></span></h1>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>For scenario choice, the feature vector can be enriched before
processing RF predictions (default option that can be disabled) by values of
the <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>d</i> axes of a linear discriminant
analysis (LDA) processed on the above summary statistics (with <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>d</i> equal to the number of scenarios minus
1; <span class=SpellE>Pudlo</span> et al. 2016). In the same spirit, for
parameter estimation, the feature vector can be completed (default option that
can be disabled) by values of a subset of the <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:
normal'>s</i> axes of a Partial Least Squares Regression analysis (PLS) also
processed on the above summary statistics (with <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:
normal'>s</i> equal to the number of summary statistics). The number of PLS
axes added to the feature vector is determined as the number of PLS axes
providing a given fraction of the maximum amount of variance explained by all
PLS axes (i.e., 95% by default, but this parameter can be adjusted). Note that,
according to our own experience on this issue, the addition into the feature
vector of LDA or PLS axes better extract genetic information from the training
set and hence globally improved statistical inferences. While the inferential
gain turned out to be systematic and substantial for LDA axes (scenario
choice), we found that including PLS axes improved parameter estimation in a
heterogeneous way, with a negligible gain in some cases (e.g. Collin et al.
2020).</span></span></p>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a name="_Toc62127951"><span
lang=EN-US>3.2 Prediction using Random Forest: scenario choice</span></a></span></h1>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>For scenario choice, the outcome of the first step of RF prediction
applied to a given target dataset is a <u>classification vote for each scenario</u>
which represents the number of times a scenario is selected in a forest of <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>n</i> trees. The scenario with the highest
classification vote corresponds to the scenario best suited to the target
dataset among the set of compared scenarios. This first RF predictor is good
enough to select the most likely scenario but not to derive directly the
associated posterior probabilities. A second analytical step based on a second
Random Forest in regression is necessary to provide an estimation of the <u>posterior
probability of the best supported scenario</u> (<span class=SpellE>Pudlo</span>
et al. 2016). </span></span></p>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a name="_Toc62127952"><span
lang=EN-US>3.3 Prediction using Random Forest: parameter estimation</span></a></span></h1>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>For parameter estimation, <span class=SpellE>Raynal</span> et al.
(2019) extended the RF approach developed in the context of (non-parametric)
regression to estimate the posterior distributions of a given parameter under a
given scenario. The approach requires the derivation of a new Random Forest for
each component of interest of the parameter vector (i.e. &#8220;one parameter,
one forest strategy&#8221;; <span class=SpellE>Raynal</span> et al. 2019).
Quite often, practitioners of Bayesian inference report the posterior mean,
posterior variance or posterior quantiles, rather than the full posterior
distribution, since the former are easier to interpret than the latter. We
implemented in DIYABC Random Forest the methodologies detailed in <span
class=SpellE>Raynal</span> et al. (2019) to provide estimations of the <u>posterior
mean, variance, median (i.e. 50% quantile) as well as 5% and 95% quantiles (and
hence 90% credibility interval) of each parameter of interest</u>. The
posterior distribution of each parameter of interest is also inferred using
importance weights following <span class=SpellE>Meinshausen</span>
(2006)&#8217;s work on quantile regression forests.</span></span></p>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a name="_Toc62127953"><span
lang=EN-US>3.4 Assessing the quality of predictions</span></a><span lang=EN-US>
</span></span></h1>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>To evaluate the robustness of inferences, DIYABC Random Forest
provides:</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:39.0pt;text-indent:-36.0pt;mso-list:
l18 level1 lfo14'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>(i)<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Global (i.e. prior)
error/accuracy indices corresponding to prediction quality measures computed <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>over the entire data space</i>;</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:39.0pt;text-indent:-36.0pt;mso-list:
l18 level1 lfo14'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='mso-bidi-font-family:Cambria;mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-latin'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>(ii)<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Local (i.e. posterior)
error/accuracy indices computed conditionally on the observed dataset and hence
corresponding to prediction quality <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>exactly
at the position of the observed dataset</i>. </span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:3.0pt'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>Note that the program used the out-of-bag prediction method for
estimating global and local error/accuracy measures (<span class=SpellE>Pudlo</span>
et al. 2016; <span class=SpellE>Raynal</span> et al. 2019; <span class=SpellE>Chapuis</span>
et al. 2020). This method is computationally efficient as it makes use of the
datasets already present in the training set and hence avoids the
(computationally costly) simulations of additional test datasets.</span></span></p>

<h3 style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:10.0pt;margin-left:
2.85pt'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a
name="_Toc62127954"><span lang=EN-US>3.4.1 Indices for scenario choice</span></a></span></h3>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l42 level1 lfo15'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><u><span lang=EN-US>Global prior errors</span></u><span
lang=EN-US> including the <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>confusion
matrix</i> (i.e. the contingency table of the true and predicted classes
&#8211; here scenarios - for each example in the training set) and the <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>mean misclassification error rate</i> (over
all scenarios).</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l42 level1 lfo15'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><u><span lang=EN-US>Local posterior error</span></u><span
lang=EN-US> which corresponds to 1 minus the posterior probability of the
selected scenario (<span class=SpellE>Chapuis</span> et al. 2020). </span></span></p>

<h3 style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:10.0pt;margin-left:
2.85pt'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a
name="_Toc62127955"><span lang=EN-US>3.4.2 Indices for parameter estimation</span></a></span></h3>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l1 level1 lfo16'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><u><span lang=EN-US>Global (prior) and local
(posterior) NMAE</span></u><span lang=EN-US> (i.e. normalized mean absolute
error): it is the average absolute difference between the point estimate and
the true simulated value divided by the true simulated value, with the mean or
the median taken as point estimate.</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l1 level1 lfo16'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><u><span lang=EN-US>Global (prior) and local
(posterior) MSE and NMSE</span></u><span lang=EN-US> (i.e. the mean square
error): it is the average squared difference between the point estimate and the
true simulated value for MSE, divided by the true simulated value for NMSE,
again with the mean or the median taken as point estimate.</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l1 level1 lfo16'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><u><span lang=EN-US>Several confidence interval
measures</span></u><span lang=EN-US> computed only at the global (prior) scale:</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>- <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>90% coverage</i>: it is the
proportion of true simulated values located between the estimated 5% and 95%
quantiles.</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>- <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Mean or median of the 90%
amplitude</i>: it is the mean or median of the difference between the estimated
5% and 95% quantiles.</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt'><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>- <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Mean or median of the
relative 90% amplitude</i>: it is the mean or median of the difference between
the estimated 5% and 95% divided by the true simulated value.</span></span></p>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a name="_Toc62127956"><span
lang=EN-US>4. PRACTICAL CONSIDERATIONS FOR ABC-RF TREATMENTS</span></a></span></h1>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>Random Forest is often (positively) considered as a
&#8220;tuning-free&#8221; method in the sense that it does not require
meticulous calibrations. This represents an important advantage of this method,
especially for non-expect users. In practice, we nevertheless advise users to
consider several checking points, thereafter formalized as questions, before
finalizing inferential treatments using DIYABC Random Forest v1.0.</span></span></p>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a name="_Toc62127957"><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:14.0pt'>4.1 Are my scenarios and/or associated
priors compatible with the observed dataset?</span></a></span><span
style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:14.0pt'><o:p></o:p></span></span></h1>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>This question is of prime interest and applies to ABC-RF as well as
to any alternative ABC treatments. This issue is particularly crucial, given
that complex scenarios and high dimensional datasets (i.e., large and hence
very informative datasets) are becoming the norm in population genomics.
Basically, if none of the proposed scenario / prior combinations produces some
simulated datasets in a reasonable vicinity of the observed dataset, this is a
signal of incompatibility and it is not recommended to attempt any inferences.
In such situations, we strongly advise reformulating the compared scenarios
and/or the associated prior distributions in order to achieve some
compatibility in the above sense. DIYABC Random Forest v1.0 proposes a visual
way to address this issue through the simultaneous projection of datasets of
the training database and of the observed dataset on the first Linear
Discriminant Analysis (LDA) axes. In the LDA projection, the (target) observed
dataset has to be reasonably located within the clouds of simulated datasets.
The program also proposes some complementary dedicated tools: (<span
class=SpellE>i</span>) a Principal Component Analysis (PCA) representing on
2-axes plans the simulated dataset from the training set and the observed
dataset; and (ii), <u>for each summary statistics</u>, the proportion of
simulated data (considering the total training set) that have a value below the
value of the observed dataset. A star indicates proportions lower than 5% or
greater than 95% (two stars, &lt;1% or &gt;1%; three stars, &lt;0.1% or &gt;0.1%).
The latter numerical results can help users to reformulating the compared
scenarios and/or the associated prior distributions in order to achieve some
compatibility (see e.g. <span class=SpellE>Cornuet</span> et al. 2010).</span></span></p>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a name="_Toc62127958"><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:14.0pt'>4.2 Did I simulate enough datasets for my
training set?</span></a></span><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:14.0pt'><o:p></o:p></span></span></h1>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>A rule of thumb is, for scenario choice to simulate between 2,000
and 20,000 datasets per scenario among those compared (<span class=SpellE>Pudlo</span>
et al. 2016; Estoup et al. 2018), and for parameter estimation to simulate
between 10,000 and 100,000 datasets under a given scenario (<span class=SpellE>Raynal</span>
et al. 2019; <span class=SpellE>Chapuis</span> et al. 2020). To evaluate
whether or not this number is sufficient for RF analysis, we recommend to
compute error/accuracy metrics such as those proposed by DIYABC Random Forest
v1.0 from both the entire training set and a subset of the latter (for instance
from a subset of 80,000 simulated datasets if the training set includes a total
of 100,000 simulated datasets). If error (accuracy) metrics from the subset are
similar, or only slightly higher (lower) than the value obtained from the
entire database, one can consider that the training set contains enough
simulated datasets. If a substantial difference is observed between both
values, then we recommend increasing the number of simulated datasets in the
training set.</span></span></p>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a name="_Toc62127959"><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:14.0pt'>4.3 Did my forest grow enough trees?</span></a></span><span
style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:14.0pt'><o:p></o:p></span></span></h1>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><span
lang=EN-US>According to our experience, a forest made of 500 to 2,000 trees
often constitutes an interesting trade-off between computation efficiency and
statistical precision (<span class=SpellE>Breiman</span>, 2001; <span
class=SpellE>Chapuis</span> et al. 2020; <span class=SpellE>Pudlo</span> et al.
2016; <span class=SpellE>Raynal</span> et al. 2019). To evaluate whether or not
this number is sufficient, we recommend plotting error/accuracy metrics as a
function of the number of trees in the forest. The shapes of the curves provide
a visual diagnostic of whether such key metrics stabilize when the number of
trees tends to a given value. DIYABC Random Forest v1.0 provides such a
plot-figure as output.</span></span><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:16.0pt;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-bidi-font-family:Calibri;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'><o:p></o:p></span></b></span></p>

<h1><span style='mso-bookmark:the-graphic-user-interface'><a name="_Toc62127960"><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria",serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin'>5. RUNNING (EXAMPLE) DATASET TREATMENTS USING
THE GRAPHIC USER INTERFACE</span></a></span><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127960'><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria",serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin'> (GUI)</span></span><span lang=EN-US
style='font-family:"Cambria",serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-hansi-theme-font:
minor-latin'><o:p></o:p></span></h1>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:10.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:
0cm;margin-left:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-pagination:widow-orphan lines-together;
page-break-after:avoid;mso-outline-level:2'><a name="doc_newSNPProjectButton"></a><a
name="_Toc62127961"><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:14.0pt;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:
major-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:major-fareast;
mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;color:#4F81BD;
mso-themecolor:accent1'>5.1 Launching the GUI</span></b></span></a><span
style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><b><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:14.0pt;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:
major-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:major-fareast;
mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;color:#4F81BD;
mso-themecolor:accent1'><o:p></o:p></span></b></span></p>

<ul style='margin-top:0cm' type=disc>
 <li class=MsoNormal style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1;margin-top:9.0pt;
     margin-bottom:9.0pt;mso-list:l14 level1 lfo42'><span style='mso-bookmark:
     doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span lang=EN-US>The GUI is the standard and
     user-friendly interface to use the software DIYABC-RF. You can configure
     the required parameters and follow the progress directly in the interface
     and through log files. A given GUI session (i.e. a window) allows working
     on a single project. You can launch several GUI sessions (i.e. several
     windows) on a single computer hence allowing working on several projects
     in parallel. <o:p></o:p></span></span></li>
 <li class=MsoNormal style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1;margin-top:9.0pt;
     margin-bottom:9.0pt;mso-list:l14 level1 lfo42'><span style='mso-bookmark:
     doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span lang=EN-US>When using the operating system
     Microsoft Windows, launch the GUI by double-clicking on <s>the icon of </s>the
     file DIYABC-RF_GUI.bat included in the DIYABC-RF_GUI_xxx_windows.zip file
     available from </span></span><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'></span><a
     href="https://diyabc.github.io/"><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span
     lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;color:black;
     mso-themecolor:text1;text-decoration:none;text-underline:none'>h</span></span></a><span
     style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'></span><a
     href="https://diyabc.github.io/"><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span
     lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;color:black;
     mso-themecolor:text1;text-decoration:none;text-underline:none'>ttps://diyabc.github.io</span></span></a><span
     style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span lang=EN-US
     style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> </span><span lang=EN-US>.
     When using MacOS, launch the GUI by double-clicking on the icon of the
     file DIYABC-<span class=SpellE>RF_GUI.command</span> included in the
     DIYABC-RF_GUI_xxx_macos.zip file available from </span></span><span
     style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'></span><a
     href="https://diyabc.github.io/"><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span
     lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;color:black;
     mso-themecolor:text1;text-decoration:none;text-underline:none'>https://diyabc.github.io</span></span></a><span
     style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span lang=EN-US> <o:p></o:p></span></span></li>
</ul>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span
lang=EN-US style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>It is worth stressing that
the program can also be run locally as any shiny application using R (only
possibility on Linux). You can visit </span></span><a
href="https://diyabc.github.io/gui/#r-package-installation"><span
style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span lang=EN-US style='color:
black;mso-themecolor:text1;text-decoration:none;text-underline:none'>https://diyabc.github.io/gui/#r-package-installation</span></span></a><span
style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span lang=EN-US style='color:
black;mso-themecolor:text1'> for more details. <o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span
lang=EN-US style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>The main pipeline of
DIYABC-RF includes two <s>main</s> modules corresponding to the two main
phases:<o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<ul style='margin-top:0cm' type=disc>
 <li class=MsoNormal style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1;margin-top:9.0pt;
     margin-bottom:9.0pt;mso-list:l29 level1 lfo40'><span style='mso-bookmark:
     doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span lang=EN-US>Module 1 = &#8220;<u>Training
     set simulation</u>&#8221; where users specify how simulated data will be
     generated under the ABC framework to produce a training set.<o:p></o:p></span></span></li>
</ul>

<ul style='margin-top:0cm' type=disc>
 <li class=MsoNormal style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1;margin-top:9.0pt;
     margin-bottom:9.0pt;mso-list:l7 level1 lfo41'><span style='mso-bookmark:
     doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span lang=EN-US>Module 2 = &#8220;<u>Random
     Forest analysis</u>&#8221; (necessitating the presence of a training set)
     which guides users through scenario choice and parameter inference by
     providing a simple interface for the supervised learning framework based
     on Random Forest methodologies.<span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></span></li>
</ul>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span
lang=EN-US style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>An additional (auxiliary)
module named &#8220;<u>Synthetic data file generation</u>&#8221; is also
available from the GUI (cf. section 8). It can be used to easily generate data
file(s) corresponding to synthetic &#8220;ground truth&#8221; raw data (not
summarized through statistics) under a given historical scenario and a set of
fixed parameter values, for instance for benchmarking purpose. The formats of
such simulated data files are the same as those described in section 7.1 for
observed (i.e. real) datasets for which one usually wants to make inferences.<o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:10.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:
0cm;margin-left:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-pagination:widow-orphan lines-together;
page-break-after:avoid;mso-outline-level:2'><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><a
name="_Toc62127962"></a><a name="doc_openProjectButton"><span style='mso-bookmark:
_Toc62127962'><b><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:14.0pt;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:major-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'>5.2 What is a DIYABC Random Forest
project?</span></b></span></a></span><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:14.0pt;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:
major-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:major-fareast;
mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;color:#4F81BD;
mso-themecolor:accent1'><o:p></o:p></span></b></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span
lang=EN-US style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>A DIYABC-RF project
consists of different files, related to the training set simulation and random
forest analyses. A project includes at least one <u>observed dataset</u> and
one <u>header file</u> associated to a (already generated or not) <u>training
set</u>. The header file, always named </span></span><span style='mso-bookmark:
doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:
12.0pt;font-family:Consolas;color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>headerRF.txt</span><span
lang=EN-US style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>, contains all information
necessary to compute a training set associated with the data: i.e. the
scenarios, the scenario parameter priors, the characteristics of loci, the loci
parameter priors and the list of summary statistics to compute using the <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Training set simulation</i> module. As soon
as the first records of the training set have been simulated, they are saved in
the training set file, always named </span></span><span style='mso-bookmark:
doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span class=SpellE><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:
11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Consolas;color:black;mso-themecolor:
text1'>reftableRF.bin</span></span><span lang=EN-US style='color:black;
mso-themecolor:text1'>. In addition, the file statobs</span></span><span
style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:
11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Consolas;color:black;mso-themecolor:
text1'>RF.txt</span><span lang=EN-US style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>,
stores the value of the summary statistics computed from the observed dataset.<o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span
lang=EN-US style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>Outputs of Random forest
analyses are available in sub-directories (each one corresponding to a specific
setting that you may have configured for the random forest analyses) in the
project directory (please see the corresponding section 7.3 for more details
regarding the content of outputs generated by a Random Forest analysis).<o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span
lang=EN-US style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>It is worth stressing that
you need to SAVE a project to avoid losing your work before quitting the GUI. A
project zip file will be generated and can be saved. If you want to later
continue with a project, or clone/modify an existing project, you can provide
an existing project zip file in the GUI when starting a project.<o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><span
lang=EN-US style='color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>Finally, we strongly
advised NOT to manually edit project-related files, unless you know what you
are doing!<o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<h2><span style='mso-bookmark:doc_newSNPProjectButton'><a name="_Toc62127963"><span
lang=EN-US>5.3 Main options of the home screen</span></a></span></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>When launching the GUI, the home
screen appears like this:</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt'><span style='mso-ansi-language:

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>The different
options proposed are self-meaning. Default values can be changed by the user.
Note that the loop-size option corresponds to the number of simulated datasets
distributed over all computer threads and stored in RAM before writing them
into the training set file (<span class=SpellE>reftableRF.bin</span>).</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127964"><span lang=EN-US>5.4 How to generate a new </span></a><span
class=SpellE><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127964'><span lang=EN-US>IndSeq</span></span></span><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127964'><span lang=EN-US> SNP training set</span></span></h2>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127965"></a><a name=defining-a-new-project><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127965'><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt'>5.4.1
Step 1: defining a new </span></span></a><span class=SpellE><span
style='mso-bookmark:defining-a-new-project'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127965'><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt'>IndSeq</span></span></span></span><span
style='mso-bookmark:defining-a-new-project'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127965'><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt'> SNP project</span></span></span><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt'><o:p></o:p></span></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>Defining a new project requires
different steps which are not strictly the same whether the data are
microsatellites/DNA sequences (MSS) or SNP (<span class=SpellE>IndSeq</span> or
<span class=SpellE>PoolSeq</span>). Let&#8217;s start with an <span
class=SpellE>IndSeq</span> SNP project. Click on the &#8220;Start&#8221; button
in the middle of the Home panel (or on the &#8220;DIYABC-RF main
pipeline&#8221; button). The following panel appears.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:
FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_32" o:spid="_x0000_i1059"
 type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:555.6pt;height:312.6pt;visibility:visible;
 mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image079.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=741 height=417
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image080.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_32"><![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l6 level1 lfo32'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;
mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Enter and validate a project
name in the &#8220;Project name&#8221; window (here <span class=SpellE>IndSeq_demonstration_project</span>)</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l6 level1 lfo32'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;
mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Select the Data type including
the locus type (<span class=SpellE>Microsat</span>/sequence or SNP) and the
sequencing mode (for SNP only; <span class=SpellE>IndSeq</span> or <span
class=SpellE>PoolSeq</span>). Here select SNP and Individual Seq.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l6 level1 lfo32'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;
mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Select the &#8220;New
project&#8221; button as we want to implement a new project from scratch.</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127966"><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt'>5.4.2 Step
2: choosing the data file</span></a><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt'><o:p></o:p></span></h2>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l27 level1 lfo26'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Choose a data file (an <span
class=SpellE>IndSeq</span> format data file in this case) using the
&#8220;Select file&#8221; browser (here INDSNP_sim_dataset_4POP_001.snp). A
large size dataset might take some times to be uploaded and checked by the
program. A short summary of the specificities of the loaded datafile appears:
here the total number of loci (30000), the minimum allele frequency chosen for
simulation (MAF=0.05), the sex ratio indicated by the user (NM=1NF), the total
number of individuals and populations, the locus type and their corresponding
numbers (A= autosomal, M=mitochondrial&#8230;; see section 7.1 for details
about datafile format), and the number of <span class=help-block>available loci
based on the MAF criterion (here 15617 &lt;A&gt;, as14383 loci, including 0
monomorphic loci, have been filtered out by the program after scanning the
proposed observed dataset</span>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:18.0pt'><span style='mso-ansi-language:
FR;mso-fareast-language:FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_33"
 o:spid="_x0000_i1058" type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:555.6pt;height:312.6pt;
 visibility:visible;mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image081.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=741 height=417
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image082.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_33"><![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l27 level1 lfo26'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>A &#8220;Project set up is
ok&#8221; message appears at the bottom of the panel if all items have gone
correctly. You can then go the next steps by clicking on the large blue color
&#8220;Training set simulation&#8221; &#8220;+&#8221; button&#8221;. The
following panel appears.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:
FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_37" o:spid="_x0000_i1057"
 type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:555.6pt;height:312.6pt;visibility:visible;
 mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image083.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=741 height=417
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image084.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_37"><![endif]></span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127967"><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt'>5.4.3 Step
3: Inform the Historical model</span></a><a name=inform-the-historical-model></a><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt'><o:p></o:p></span></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>Click on the &#8220;Add&#8221; button
of the &#8220;Define historical models&#8221; section. The following panel
appears:</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:
FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_38" o:spid="_x0000_i1056"
 type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:475.2pt;height:267.6pt;visibility:visible;
 mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image085.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=634 height=357
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image086.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_38"><![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span lang=EN-US>Write the code of a first scenario
(scenario 1) in the edit <span class=GramE>window &#8221;Describe</span> your
scenario&#8221; and click on the &#8220;Validate&#8221; button. </span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l35 level1 lfo37'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>If we click on the &#8220;Draw
scenario&#8221; button, the logic of the scenario is checked and if it is found
OK, and if the scenario is draw-able, a graphical representation of the
scenario appears. You can save it by clicking on the &#8220;Save image&#8221;
button. Figures are saved in 'fig' sub-folder in the project directory.
Possible extensions are: 'eps', '<span class=SpellE>ps</span>', '<span
class=SpellE>tex</span>', 'pdf', 'jpeg', 'tiff', '<span class=SpellE>png</span>',
'bmp', '<span class=SpellE>svg</span>'.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:
FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_42" o:spid="_x0000_i1055"
 type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:483.6pt;height:272.4pt;visibility:visible;
 mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image087.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=645 height=363
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image088.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_42"><![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l35 level1 lfo37'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The &#8220;Priors and
conditions&#8221; frame which appears below allows choosing the prior distribution
of each parameter of the scenario. A parameter is anything in the scenario that
is not a keyword (here <span class=VerbatimChar><span style='mso-ansi-font-size:
12.0pt;font-family:"Cambria",serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-hansi-theme-font:
minor-latin'>sample</span></span>, <span class=VerbatimChar><span
style='mso-ansi-font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Cambria",serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:
minor-latin;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin'>merge and split</span></span>),
nor a numeric value. In our example scenario, parameters are hence: <span
class=VerbatimChar><span style='mso-ansi-font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Cambria",serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin'>N1, N2, N3,
N4, ra, t21, t32</span></span> and <span class=VerbatimChar><span
style='mso-ansi-font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Cambria",serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:
minor-latin;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin'>t423</span></span>. We choose a
uniform distribution and change the min and max values (100 and 10000 for N
values - 10 and 1000 for t values; see panel below). </span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:
FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_43" o:spid="_x0000_i1054"
 type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:524.4pt;height:294.6pt;visibility:visible;
 mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image089.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=699 height=393
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image090.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_43"><![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l35 level1 lfo37'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span>In our example, we also need to specify
conditions for the priors on <span class=VerbatimChar><span style='mso-ansi-font-size:
12.0pt;font-family:"Cambria",serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-hansi-theme-font:
minor-latin'>t21, t32 and t432 such that </span></span>t21&gt;t32 and t32&gt;t423.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:
FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_55" o:spid="_x0000_i1053"
 type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:490.8pt;height:276pt;visibility:visible;
 mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image091.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=654 height=368
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image092.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_55"><![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span lang=EN-US>To do this we write t21&gt;t32 and t32&gt;t432
on two successive lines in the &#8220;Condition setting&#8221; frame. As noted
in the panel, conditions should have the following format: XX&lt;YY. where
&#8216;XX' and 'YY' are parameters of the same type. You can use the standard
comparison signs: '&gt;', '&gt;=', '&lt;', '=&lt;'. It is worth stressing that
the omission of such conditional constraints on merge times (cf.&nbsp;a
population needs to exist in the past to allow coalescence events in it) is one
of the most frequent implementation error made by DIYABC-RF users. If forgotten
a message &quot;Error in simulation process: check your scenarios, priors and
conditions&quot;&quot; appears. Note that the occurrence of a too large number
of time conditional constraints within a scenario may substantially slow down
simulations as a valid t parameter vector will be retain and run only once all
conditions are fulfilled.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l16 level1 lfo27'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>We then can <u>add some other
scenarios in additional windows</u> by clicking on the button &#8220;Add&#8221;
(one or several times if one wants to add a single or several other scenarios).
In the present example, we simulate datasets from six different scenarios that
we want to compare (see Collin et al. 2020 example based on pseudo-observed
datasets for details), hence the six scenario windows that we have completed
with instructions for each one. For the sixth scenario the panel looks like
this:</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:
FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_62" o:spid="_x0000_i1052"
 type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:555.6pt;height:312.6pt;visibility:visible;
 mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image093.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=741 height=417
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image094.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_62"><![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR'>Complete time
conditions for the six scenarios <span class=GramE>are:</span> t21&gt;t32,
t42&lt;t21, t43&lt;t32, t32&gt;t423, t431&lt;t32 and t421&lt;t21<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:10.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:
0cm;margin-left:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-pagination:widow-orphan lines-together;
page-break-after:avoid;mso-outline-level:2'><a name="_Toc62127968"><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:major-latin;
mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:major-fareast;
mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;color:#4F81BD;
mso-themecolor:accent1'>5.4.4 Step 4: Inform number of loci to simulate (and
chromosome type)</span></b></a><b><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:major-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>Choose the number of SNP locus that you
want to simulate for each chromosome type define in the data file (<i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>A</i> for autosomal diploid loci, <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>H</i> for autosomal haploid loci, <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>X</i> for X-linked or haplo-diploid loci,<i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'> Y</i> for Y-linked loci and <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>M</i> for mitochondrial loci; see section
7.1.1). Here we have only type &lt;A&gt; SNP loci. According to our own
experience, analyzing (evolutionary neutral) scenarios using 5000 to 20000 SNP
loci is sufficient to obtain robust results. In this example, we choose to
consider simulations based on a subset of 5000 SNP loci (with MAF=0.05 as
indicated previously) taken in order from the <u>first</u> SNP locus of the
data file, by replacing 30000 by 5000 in the corresponding frame. Click on the
button &#8220;Validate&#8221;. </span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>It is worth stressing that choosing a
subset of 5000 SNP loci taken from the SNP locus 5001 of the data file would
lead to a training set generated from a set of 5000 loci completely independent
from the previous one. Generating by this way different training sets is a way
to process independent analyses of a given dataset (a sufficiently large number
of SNP loci available in the observed dataset is obviously needed to do that).</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:
FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_68" o:spid="_x0000_i1051"
 type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:531.6pt;height:298.8pt;visibility:visible;
 mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image095.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=709 height=398
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image096.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_68"><![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:10.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:
0cm;margin-left:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-pagination:widow-orphan lines-together;
page-break-after:avoid;mso-outline-level:2'><a name="_Toc62127969"><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:major-latin;
mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:major-fareast;
mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;color:#4F81BD;
mso-themecolor:accent1'>5.4.5 Step 5: Summary statistics</span></b></a><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:major-latin;
mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:major-fareast;
mso-hansi-theme-font:major-latin;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;color:#4F81BD;
mso-themecolor:accent1'><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US>In the present
version of the program, all available summary statistics are computed as
mentioned in the interface below the &#8220;Summary statistics&#8221; item (see
previous panel-copy) and as detailed when clicking on the button &#8220;?&#8221;
on the right:<span style='color:red;background:yellow;mso-highlight:yellow'><o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>For both <span class=SpellE>IndSeq</span> and <span class=SpellE>PoolSeq</span>
SNP loci, the following set of summary statistics has been implemented.<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US>1. <span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Proportion of monomorphic loci</i> for each
population, as well as for each pair and triplet of populations (ML1p, ML2p,
ML3p)</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>Mean and variance (over loci) values are computed for all subsequent
summary statistics. <o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US>2. <span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Heterozygosity</i> for each population (HW)
and for each pair of populations (HB)</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US>3.<span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>FST</i>-<i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>related
statistics</i> for each population (FST1), for each pair (FST2), triplet
(FST3), quadruplet (FST4) and overall (FSTG) populations (when the dataset
includes more than four populations)</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US>4. <span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Patterson&#8217;s f-statistics</i> for each
triplet (f3-statistics; F3) and quadruplet (f4-statistics; F4) of populations </span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US>5. <span
style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span
class=SpellE><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Nei&#8217;s</i></span><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'> distance</i> (NEI) for each pair of
populations</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US>6. <span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Maximum likelihood coefficient of admixture</i>
(AML) computed for each triplet of populations.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:35.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-33.0pt'><span
lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:2.85pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt'><span lang=EN-US>Note the short code
name for each type of summary statistics (MLP1p, HW, FST2, F<span class=GramE>3,&#8230;</span>).
Such code names of statistics (plus the suffix m and v for mean and variance
over loci, respectively; see section 2.6.3) will be used in most files produced
by the program, including the key files headerRF.txt, <span class=SpellE>reftableRF.bin</span>
and statobsRF.txt.</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127970"></a><a name=building-the-reference-table><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc62127970'><span lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt'>5.4.6
Step 6: Simulate the training set</span></span></a><span lang=EN-US
style='font-size:12.0pt'><o:p></o:p></span></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>You can access the &#8220;training set
simulation&#8221; module by clicking on the corresponding + button on the far
right of the box blue title bar &#8220;Training set simulation&#8221;. The
following &#8220;Run&#8221; panel appears.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:
FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_69" o:spid="_x0000_i1050"
 type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:555.6pt;height:312.6pt;visibility:visible;
 mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image097.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=741 height=417
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image098.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_69"><![endif]><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span></span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;
mso-list:l20 level1 lfo24'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Indicate the required number of
datasets to simulate in the training set: we here change the default value of
100 into 12000 (in order to simulate 2000 datasets for each of the six
scenarios)</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l20 level1 lfo24'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>Launch the generation of the
simulated datasets of the training set by clicking on the large blue color
button &#8220;Simulate&#8221;. The number of datasets already simulated is
given in the &#8220;Running simulation&#8221; progress bar below.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l32 level1 lfo25'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>You can stop the generation of
simulated datasets by clicking on the &#8220;STOP&#8221; button. Both a &#8220;Run
succeeded&#8221; message appears when all requested simulations have been
processed.</span></p>

<p class=MsoListParagraph style='text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l32 level1 lfo25'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><u><span lang=EN-US>Do not forget to click on
the &#8220;Save&#8221; button in the &#8220;Project administration&#8221; lower
panel to implement and save a concatenated zip file including various input and
output files</span></u><span lang=EN-US> (see section 7 for a description of
the content of some of those files) on your computer. The name of the
implemented/saved concatenated .zip file is the one given at the start in the
&#8220;Project name&#8221; window (here <span class=SpellE>IndSeq_demonstration_project</span>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:
FR;mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_70" o:spid="_x0000_i1049"
