<h2><a name="_Toc62127986"><span lang=EN-US>7.2 Training set file(s)</span></a><a
name=reference-table-files></a></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>Training set files are binary files
which include two successive parts:</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo11'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The first file is a header
(named <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>headerRF.txt</b>) which contains
information necessary to read the second part (file), such as the number of
scenarios, or the number of parameters of each scenario.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-left:24.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo11'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The second file (named <span
class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>reftableRF.bin</b></span>)
corresponds to the training set per se, as this file contains simulated dataset
records, each record containing on the same line the scenario number, the
parameter values and summary statistics values.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>Each time a training set (<span
class=SpellE>reftableRF.bin</span>) is created or increased (each time the
training set &#8220;Run&#8221; button is pressed), two text files are created
in the project directory:</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l22 level1 lfo33'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:
Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>statobsRF.txt</span></b><span lang=EN-US>: this text file contains
the values of summary statistics for the observed data set.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;
mso-list:l22 level1 lfo33'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US
style='font-family:Symbol;mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:
Symbol'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span class=VerbatimChar><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'><span lang=EN-US style='mso-ansi-font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Cambria",serif;
mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin'>first_records_of_the_reference_table_X.txt</span></b></span><span
lang=EN-US> in which <span class=VerbatimChar><span style='mso-ansi-font-size:
12.0pt;font-family:"Cambria",serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-hansi-theme-font:
minor-latin'>X</span></span> is an integer number starting at 0 and increasing
each time the training set &#8220;Run&#8221; button is pressed. This file
provides a text version of the first </span><!--[if gte msEquation 12]><m:oMath><i
 style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>n</m:r></span></i></m:oMath><![endif]--><![if !msEquation]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:
minor-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";
mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-bidi;position:relative;top:2.5pt;mso-text-raise:-2.5pt;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape
 id="_x0000_i1025" type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:7.2pt;height:22.8pt'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image181.png"
  o:title="" chromakey="white"/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img width=10 height=30
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image182.gif" v:shapes="_x0000_i1025"><![endif]></span><![endif]><span
lang=EN-US><span style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span>newly created records of
the training set reftableRF.bin (</span><!--[if gte msEquation 12]><m:oMath><i
 style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Cambria Math",serif'><m:r>n</m:r></span></i></m:oMath><![endif]--><![if !msEquation]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:12.0pt;font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-ascii-theme-font:
minor-latin;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:minor-latin;
mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-bidi-font-family:"Times New Roman";
mso-bidi-theme-font:minor-bidi;position:relative;top:2.5pt;mso-text-raise:-2.5pt;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape
 id="_x0000_i1025" type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:7.2pt;height:22.8pt'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image181.png"
  o:title="" chromakey="white"/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img width=10 height=30
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image182.gif" v:shapes="_x0000_i1025"><![endif]></span><![endif]><span
lang=EN-US><span style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp;</span>being equal to the <i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Particle loop size</i>, see section 3.7.3).</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127987"><span lang=EN-US>7.3 Output files produced by a
Random Forest analysis</span></a><a name=output-files></a></h2>

<p class=MsoNormal><span lang=EN-US>DIYABC Random Forest provides various
numerical and graphical outputs. The integration of the various graphical
outputs is managed with the ggplot2 R package (Wickham 2016), allowing user to
create and export high-quality graphics related to the analyses. Non-graphical
outputs are saved in text files. Graphs are saved as images, and user can
choose the image format among <span class=SpellE>png</span>, jpg, etc. Once a
Random Forest analysis is terminated, do not forget to click on the
&#8220;Save&#8221; button in the &#8220;Project housekeeping&#8221; panel to
implement and save a concatenated .zip file including various input and output
files (see section 7 for a description of the content of some of those files)
on your computer. The name of the implemented/saved concatenated .zip file is
the one given at the start in the &#8220;Project name&#8221; window.</span></p>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>We now describe all the files produced
by each Random Forest analysis.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span lang=EN-US>abcranger_call.log</span></b><span
lang=EN-US>: log files with votes and posterior probability of the selected (i.e.
best) scenario (i.e. model) for a model choice analysis and with the main
outputs of parameter estimation (including predictions and accuracy of
estimation indices) for a parameter estimation analysis.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><u><span lang=EN-US><o:p><span style='text-decoration:
 none'>&nbsp;</span></o:p></span></u></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><u><span lang=EN-US>Scenario choice analysis<o:p></o:p></span></u></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l5 level1 lfo30'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;
mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>Numerical outputs<o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>modelchoice_out.settings</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>: this
file summarizes the settings associated to the RF analysis processed for
scenario choice.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>modelchoice_out.confusion</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>: mean
misclassification error rate and confusion matrix (i.e. the contingency table
of the true and predicted classes for each example in the training set). These
indices are computed using the out-of-bag (a.k.a. out-of-bootstrap or <span
class=SpellE>oob</span>) training data as free test dataset.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>modelchoice_out.predictions</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>: votes,
prediction of the selected scenario and posterior probability of the selected
scenario (i.e. model).</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>modelchoice_<span class=GramE>out.ooberror</span></span></b></span><span
lang=EN-US>: Evolution of prediction power relatively to the number of trees in
the forest. Line number is the number of trees. Power is the global (prior)
error rate for scenario choice with the mean taken as point estimate (computed
using <span class=SpellE>oob</span>). See the file
modelchoice_out_graph_error_versus_ntrees.png for a graphical representation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>modelchoice_out.importance</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>:
variables importance (sorted) which correspond to the contributions of the
statistics to the Random Forest when choosing among scenarios. The variable
importance of each statistics is computed as the mean decrease of impurity
across the trees, where the impurity measure is the Gini index. Note that the
scale is irrelevant: only the relative values matter. The variable importance
was computed for each of the summary statistics provided by DIYABC Random
Forest, plus the LDA axes (denoted LDA) if they have been added to the feature
vector. The higher the variable importance the more informative is the
statistic. Variable importance of noise variables (denoted <span class=SpellE>NOISEx</span>
and corresponding to values randomly drawn into uniform distributions bounded
between 0 and 1) are also provided. Such noise variable can be added to the
feature vector processed by RF in order to evaluate the threshold of variable
importance values below which components of the vector are not informative
anymore. More details about summary statistics including their code names can
be found in section 2.6.3. Population index(s) are also indicated at the end of
each statistic. See Collin et al. 2020 for examples. See the file
modelchoice_out_graph_variable_importance.png for a graphical representation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>modelchoice_out.lda</span></b></span><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'><span lang=EN-US>:</span></b><span lang=EN-US><span
style='mso-spacerun:yes'>&nbsp; </span>coordinates for the projection of the
datasets from the training set and from the observed dataset on the first two
linear discriminant analysis (LDA) axes when analyzing more than two scenarios
(models) and on a single LDA axis when analyzing a pair of scenarios (or two
groups of scenarios); See the file modelchoice_out_graph_lda.png for a
graphical representation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l5 level1 lfo30'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;
mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>Graphical outputs</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span lang=EN-US>modelchoice_out_graph_lda.png:</span></b><span
lang=EN-US> Projection of the datasets from the training set on the first two
linear discriminant analysis (LDA) axes when analyzing more than two scenarios
(models) and on a single LDA axis when analyzing a pair of scenarios (or two
groups of scenarios). The location of the observed dataset in the LDA
projection is indicated by a star symbol or a vertical line. Graphical
representation obtained from the text file <span class=SpellE>modelchoice_out.lda</span>;
see also Figure 2 in Collin et al. 2020.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span lang=EN-US>modelchoice_out_graph_error_versus_ntrees.png:</span></b><span
lang=EN-US> Evolution of prediction power relatively to the number of trees in
the forest. Graphical representation obtained from the text file <span
class=SpellE>modelchoice_<span class=GramE>out.ooberror</span></span> ; see
also Figure S1 in Collin et al. 2020.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span lang=EN-US>modelchoice_out_graph_variable_importance.png:</span></b><span
lang=EN-US> Contributions of the 50 most informative statistics (including LDA
axes if computed) to the Random Forest when choosing among scenarios. Graphical
representation obtained from the text file <span class=SpellE>modelchoice_out.importance</span>;
see also Figure 3 in Collin et al. 2020.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span lang=EN-US><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><u><span lang=EN-US>Parameter estimation analysis<o:p></o:p></span></u></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l5 level1 lfo30'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;
mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>Numerical outputs<o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>estim_param_out.settings</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>: this
file summarizes the settings associated to the RF analysis processed to
estimate a given parameter</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>estim_param_out.predictions</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>:
expectation, median, quantiles 0.05, quantile 0.95, and variance for prediction
of parameter estimation</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>estim_param_<span class=GramE>out.ooberror</span></span></b></span><span
lang=EN-US>: Evolution of prediction power relatively to the number of trees in
the forest. Line number is the number of trees. Power is the global (prior)
mean squared error with the mean taken as point estimate (computed using <span
class=SpellE>oob</span>). See the file
estim_param_out_graph_error_versus_ntrees.png for a graphical representation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>estim_param_out.oobstats</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>: this
file contains various accuracy indices of parameter estimation (computed using <span
class=SpellE>oob</span>). Both global (prior) error indices and Local
(posterior) error indices are provided (see Collin et al. 2020 for details).</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>estim_param_out.importance</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>:
variables importance (sorted) which correspond to the contributions of the
statistics to the Random Forest when processing parameter estimation. The
variable importance of each statistics is computed as the mean decrease of
impurity across the trees, where the impurity measure is the residual sum of
squares. Note that the scale is irrelevant: only the relative values matter.
The variable importance was computed for each of the summary statistics
provided by DIYABC Random Forest, plus the PLS axes (denoted Comp.) if they
have been added to the feature vector. The higher the variable importance the
more informative is the statistic. Variable importance of noise variables
(denoted <span class=SpellE>NOISEx</span> and corresponding to values randomly
drawn into uniform distributions bounded between 0 and 1) are also provided.
Such noise variable can be added to the feature vector processed by RF in order
to evaluate the threshold of variable importance values below which components
of the vector are not informative anymore. More details about summary
statistics including their code names can be found in section 2.6.3. Population
index(s) are also indicated at the end of each statistic. See Collin et al.
2020 for examples. See the file estim_param_out_graph_variable_importance.png
for a graphical representation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>estim_param_out.predweights</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>:
pairs of parameter value - weight value inferred during prediction. Such
pairwise values can be used to do density plot of parameter estimation. See the
file estim_param_out_graph_density_plot.png for a graphical representation.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US>If
a Partial Least Squares Regression analysis (PLS) is processed on the summary
statistics then two additional output files are provided.<o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>estim_param_out.plsvar</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>: variance
explained by number of the <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>c</i> selected
PLS components (from component 1 to <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>c,</i>
with c the number of PLS axes providing a given fraction of the maximum amount
of variance explained by all PLS axes - 95% by default-).</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span class=SpellE><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>estim_param_out.plsweights</span></b></span><span lang=EN-US>:
weight of each variable (i.e. summary statistics) for the first PLS component
(sorted by absolute value)</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:
l5 level1 lfo30'><![if !supportLists]><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:Symbol;
mso-fareast-font-family:Symbol;mso-bidi-font-family:Symbol'><span
style='mso-list:Ignore'>&middot;<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span
lang=EN-US>Graphical outputs</span></i></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span lang=EN-US>estim_param_out_graph_density_plot.png</span></b><span
lang=EN-US>: density plot graphical representation for the estimated parameter
(obtained from the text file <span class=SpellE>estim_param_out.predweights</span>).</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span lang=EN-US>estim_param_out_graph_error_versus_ntrees.png:</span></b><span
lang=EN-US> Evolution of prediction power relatively to the number of trees in
the forest. Graphical representation obtained from the text file <span
class=SpellE>estim_param_out.ooberror</span>; see also Figure S1 in Collin et
al. 2020.</span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span lang=EN-US>estim_param_out_graph_variable_importance.png</span></b><span
lang=EN-US>: Contributions of the 50 most informative statistics (including PLS
components &#8211; denoted as Comp - if computed) to the Random Forest when
choosing among scenarios. Graphical representation obtained from the text file <span
class=SpellE>estim_param_out.ooberror</span>; see also Figure 3 in Collin et
al. 2020.</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc62127988"><span lang=EN-US>7.4 Other files</span></a></h2>

<p class=FirstParagraph><span lang=EN-US>The program writes several additional
files in the saved project directory:</span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>diyabc_run_call.log:</span><span
lang=EN-US style='font-weight:normal'> this text file contains information
about the first steps of the training set production, including the reading of
the observed data file and the interpretation of the headerRF.txt file.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=DefinitionTerm style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>reftable.log:
</span><span lang=EN-US style='font-weight:normal'>this file contains information
about the progress of computations (achieved number of records)<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'><span lang=EN-US>RNG_state_0000.bin</span></b><span lang=EN-US>: this
binary file contains the current state of the random generator.</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'><span lang=EN-US>diyabc_seed_init_call.log: </span></b><span
lang=EN-US>this text file contains information about the initialization of the
random generator</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'><span lang=EN-US>Files produced with <span class=SpellE>IndSeq</span>
analysis</span></b><span lang=EN-US> <br>
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; - &lt;<span class=SpellE>observed_dataset_name</span>&gt;.bin
and &lt;<span class=SpellE>observed_dataset_name</span>&gt;.txt: observed
dataset file in bin and txt format, respectively <br>
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; - maf.txt: file in which the minimum allele frequency value
(<span class=SpellE>maf</span>) has been recorded</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:24.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:
0cm;margin-left:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-pagination:widow-orphan lines-together;
page-break-after:avoid;mso-outline-level:1'><a name="_Toc62127989"><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:16.0pt;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-bidi-font-family:Calibri;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'>8. GENERATE SYNTHETIC DATAFILES</span></b></a><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:16.0pt;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-bidi-font-family:Calibri;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'> </span></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:10.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>An (auxiliary)
module named &#8220;<b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>Synthetic data file
generation</b>&#8221; (based on the DIYABC simulation engine) is available in
DIYABC Random Forest v1.0. You can use this module to generate datafile(s) for
various types of genetic markers corresponding to synthetic &#8220;ground
truth&#8221; raw data (not summarized through statistics) under a given
historical scenario and a set of parameter values <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'>fixed by the user</b>. Such <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>pseudo-observed
dataset</b> does not refer to any (actual) observed dataset. <b
style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>The formats of the generated datafiles are
similar to those of the observed input datafiles read by DIYABC Random Forest
v1.0 (see sections 7.1.1, 7.1.2 and 7.1.3).</b></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span lang=EN-US>To access to the panels allowing generating
files corresponding to full in silico datasets (also called pseudo-observed
datasets) click on the &#8220;Synthetic data file generation&#8221; button in
the middle of the main panel of the GUI or on the &#8220;Synthetic data file
generation&#8221; button in the upper-left part of the same panel.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR;mso-fareast-language:FR;
mso-no-proof:yes'><!--[if gte vml 1]><v:shape id="Image_x0020_128" o:spid="_x0000_i1025"
 type="#_x0000_t75" style='width:502.8pt;height:282.6pt;visibility:visible;
 mso-wrap-style:square'>
 <v:imagedata src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image183.png"
  o:title=""/>
</v:shape><![endif]--><![if !vml]><img border=0 width=670 height=377
src="DiyabcRandomForestUserManual21-01-2021_fichiers/image184.jpg" v:shapes="Image_x0020_128"><![endif]></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal><span lang=EN-US>The panels following such clicking are very
similar to those detailed in the sections 5.4 (<span class=SpellE>IndSeq</span>
data), 5.5 (<span class=SpellE>PoolSeq</span> data) and 5.6 (microsatellite
and/or DNA sequence data). <u>Their self-meaning content allows defining a
scenario, fixing prior values for historical (and genetic) parameters, and the
number (and type) of loci to simulate</u>. Note that those panels are completed
by two (also self-meaning) additional panels in which you indicate the sample
sizes for each population (with the proportion of males and females in each
sample), the sex ratio of the studied species, and the number of datafiles that
you want to simulate.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:24.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:
0cm;margin-left:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-pagination:widow-orphan lines-together;
page-break-after:avoid;mso-outline-level:1'><a name="_Toc62127990"><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:16.0pt;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-bidi-font-family:Calibri;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'>9. USING DIYABC RANDOM FOREST ON A
COMPUTER SERVER AND EXAMPLES OF COMMAND LINES</span></b></a><a name=cluster></a></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US>The computing effort is considerably reduced
for ABC Random Forest, as the method requires a substantially smaller training
set compared to ABC methods (e.g., a few thousands of simulated datasets versus
hundreds of thousands of simulations per scenario for most ABC approaches; Blum
&amp; Fran&ccedil;ois, 2010; <span class=SpellE>Fraimout</span> et al., 2017; <span
class=SpellE>Pudlo</span> et al., 2016; <span class=SpellE>Raynal</span> et
al., 2019). Given the ever-increasing dimensionality of modern genetic data
generated using NGS technologies, this is a particularly appealing property of
this method. Your personal computer or any local server should hence represent
sufficient computer resources to run most of your DIYABC Random Forest analyses
in a descent time. However, in some cases (for instance when very large SNP
datasets have to be simulated), it might be useful to take advantage of <u>a
compute server (single node of a cluster, or even a powerful workstation),
especially to generate the training set (i.e. the file <span class=SpellE>reftableRF.bin</span>)</u>.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US>To do this (i.e. generate the <span
class=SpellE>reftableRF.bin</span> training set), go to the DIYABC Random
Forest main site <a href="https://diyabc.github.io/">https://diyabc.github.io/</a>
at the <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>Command line tools</i> section to
find</span><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;
color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'> </span><span lang=EN-US>the <span
class=SpellE>diyabc</span> v3.0 binary (executable) file corresponding to your
Operating System</span><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;
color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'>. Compilation and command line instructions
are also available </span><span lang=EN-US>at</span><span lang=EN-US
style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'> </span><span
lang=EN-US><a href="https://github.com/diyabc/diyabc"><span style='font-family:
"Times New Roman",serif'>the <span class=SpellE>github</span> repository for <span
class=SpellE>diyabc</span> RF</span></a>. </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US>Similarly, compilation, command line
instructions as well as the sources and various binary versions of the program <span
class=SpellE>abcranger</span>, which is the Random Forest inference engine of
the program DIYABC Random Forest, are also available at <a
href="https://github.com/diyabc/abcranger">the <span class=SpellE>github</span>
repository for <span class=SpellE>abcranger</span></a>. However, this might be
less crucial as</span><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>
Random Forest treatments with <span class=SpellE>abcranger</span> (using a
given training set) are much more rapid than the generation of the training set
with <span class=SpellE>diyabc</span> v3.0 (e.g. Collin et al. 2020).<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span lang=EN-US>EXAMPLES
OF COMMAND LINES <o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:Wingdings;mso-ascii-font-family:
Cambria;mso-ascii-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-hansi-font-family:Cambria;
mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:
Wingdings'><span style='mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings'>&agrave;</span></span><span
lang=EN-US>Warning: for more details and options see instructions in <a
href="https://diyabc.github.io/cli/"><span class=SpellE>Commande</span> line
tools - DIYABC RF</a> </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo44'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Wingdings;mso-fareast-font-family:Wingdings;
mso-bidi-font-family:Wingdings'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&Oslash;<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp; </span></span></span><![endif]><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US>Simulation of a training
set using the (<span class=SpellE>linux</span>) executable file <span
class=SpellE>diyabc_vXXX</span> (where XXX is the version)<o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US>Put in a given directory the following files:</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l43 level1 lfo20'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-fareast-font-family:
Calibri'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>-<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The file corresponding to your
(observed) dataset</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormalCxSpMiddle style='margin-left:36.0pt;mso-add-space:auto;
text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l43 level1 lfo20'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-fareast-font-family:
Calibri'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>-<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The header file (<u>that you
will have to name <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>header.txt</b></u> as
a headerRF.txt file will be automatically produced) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l43 level1 lfo20'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-fareast-font-family:
Calibri'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>-<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The file RNG_state_0000.bin,
which you should generate at first in a terminal window with:</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:36.0pt'><span class=GramE><span style='font-family:"Courier New";
mso-ansi-language:FR'>./</span></span><span class=SpellE><span
style='font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'>diyabc_vXXX</span></span><span
style='font-family:"Courier New";mso-ansi-language:FR'> -p ./ -n
&quot;t:8&quot;<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:36.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>where you can replace 8 by the number of
computing cores of your server.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US>You can then launch the simulation in a
terminal window with:</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span class=GramE><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Courier New"'>./</span></span><span
class=SpellE><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Courier New"'>diyabc_vXXX</span></span><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Courier New"'> -p ./ -R ALL -r 12000 -g 50 -m -t
8<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US>By doing so you will simulate of a training
set including 12000 datasets with <u>all</u> summary statistics available in <span
class=SpellE>diyabcrf</span> (plus LDA axes added to the feature vector) and
using a loop size of 50 simulated datasets and a total of 8 cores (you can
specify at most the number of cores specified by the previously generated <span
class=SpellE>RNG_state</span>_***.bin file<span class=GramE>) .</span></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo44'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:Wingdings;mso-fareast-font-family:Wingdings;
mso-bidi-font-family:Wingdings'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>&Oslash;<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp; </span></span></span><![endif]><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US>Random Forest analyses</span></i><span
lang=EN-US> <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>using the (<span
class=SpellE>linux</span>) executable file <span class=SpellE>abcranger_vXXX</span><o:p></o:p></i></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US>Put in a given directory the following files:</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l43 level1 lfo20'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-fareast-font-family:
Calibri'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>-<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The file headerRF.txt
(previously generated by <span class=SpellE>diyabc_vXXX</span>) </span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l43 level1 lfo20'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-fareast-font-family:
Calibri'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>-<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The file <span class=SpellE>reftableRF.bin</span>
(previously generated by <span class=SpellE>diyabc_vXXX</span>) corresponding
to the training set</span><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;mso-list:l43 level1 lfo20'><![if !supportLists]><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Calibri",sans-serif;mso-fareast-font-family:
Calibri'><span style='mso-list:Ignore'>-<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span></span><![endif]><span lang=EN-US>The file statobsRF.txt
(previously generated by <span class=SpellE>diyabc_vXXX</span>) which contains
the values of summary statistics for the observed data set.</span><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<ul style='margin-top:0cm' type=disc>
 <li class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-bottom:9.0pt;mso-list:l25 level1 lfo45'><span
     lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Model (scenario)
     choice using RF<o:p></o:p></span></li>
</ul>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>You
can then launch the analysis in a terminal window with:<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span class=GramE><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Courier New"'>./</span></span><span
class=SpellE><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Courier New"'>abcranger_vXXX</span></span><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Courier New"'> -n 12000 -t 1000 -j 8 -o <span
class=SpellE>modelchoice_analysis</span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>By
doing so you will process a model choice analysis on 12000 datasets of the
training set with a forest including 1000 trees, with error metrics computed
from 12000 &#8220;out-of-bag (<span class=SpellE>oob</span>) datasets, and
using a total of 8 cores. All output files names will have &#8220;<span
class=SpellE>modelchoice_analysis</span>&#8221; as prefix.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<ul style='margin-top:0cm' type=disc>
 <li class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-bottom:9.0pt;mso-list:l25 level1 lfo45'><span
     lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Parameter
     estimation (t) using RF<o:p></o:p></span></li>
</ul>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>You
can launch the analysis in a terminal window with:<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span class=GramE><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Courier New"'>./</span></span><span
class=SpellE><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Courier New"'>abcranger_vXXX</span></span><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Courier New"'> -n 2000 -t 1000 -j 8 --parameter
t --<span class=SpellE>chosenscen</span> 1 --<span class=SpellE>plsmaxvar</span>
0.95 --noob 10000 -o <span class=SpellE>estim_param_t_with_PLS</span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><span lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>By
doing so you will process an estimation of the parameter t from 2000 datasets
(if available in the training set) with a forest including 1000 trees, with a
number of PLS components explaining 95% of variance added to the feature
vector, with accuracy metrics computed from 10000 out-of-bag (<span
class=SpellE>oob</span>) datasets, and using a total of 8 cores. All output
files names will have &#8220;<span class=SpellE>estim_param_t_with_PLS</span>&#8221;
as prefix.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm'><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span lang=EN-US
style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>Note: The pipeline and command
lines used to generate and analyze the example datasets in Collin et al. (2020)
can be consulted at </span></i><span lang=EN-US><a
href="https://github.com/diyabc/MER_publication_materials/tree/main/MER_2021_DATASET_EXAMPLES"><span
style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'>https://github.com/diyabc/MER_publication_materials/tree/main/MER_2021_DATASET_EXAMPLES</span></a></span><span
lang=EN-US style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif'> <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:9.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:9.0pt;
margin-left:0cm;text-indent:36.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>It is worth stressing that
<span class=SpellE>abcranger</span> is not limited to population genetics
applications as you can use the program as a Random Forest inference engine
independently from the <span class=SpellE>diyabc</span> simulator. However, for
the moment, the binary standalone used by the DIYABC Random Forest interface
handles only outputs produced by the <span class=SpellE>diyabc</span>
simulator. A python wrapper (and example notebooks) is available at the <a
href="https://github.com/diyabc/abcranger">notebook directory in the <span
class=SpellE>github</span> repository</a></span><span lang=EN-US
style='font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;color:black;mso-themecolor:text1'> </span><span
lang=EN-US>and a R wrapper will be soon provided at the same site.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:24.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:
0cm;margin-left:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-pagination:widow-orphan lines-together;
page-break-after:avoid;mso-outline-level:1'><a name="_Toc62127991"><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:16.0pt;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-bidi-font-family:Calibri;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'>10. TOY EXAMPLES</span></b></a><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:16.0pt;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-bidi-font-family:Calibri;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=Definition style='margin-top:10.0pt;line-height:150%'><span
lang=EN-US>Five toy examples to process run-tests with DIYABC-RF (i.e. for a
quick generation of a training set and rapid Random Forest analyses) can be
downloaded from <span style='color:#0066FF'>https://diyabc.github.io/toy_examples</span>/.
Each toy example illustrates crucial aspects such as the formats of different
types of observed datasets, the formalization of different types of scenarios
and the using of various types of molecular markers. Each toy example includes
two files: <b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'>an observed dataset file and
a &#8220;ready to use&#8221; headerRF.txt file</b>. You can launch directly the
ABC-RF standalone by choosing the &#8220;Existing project&#8221; option and
loading these two files.</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'><span lang=EN-US>TOY_EXAMPLE1_microsatellites_one_pop_bottlenecked<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>The
pseudo-observed dataset includes a single population bottlenecked at time <span
class=SpellE>tbn</span> in the past with 4 samples (20 <span class=SpellE>inds</span>
per sample) taken at different times. Note that NM=1.0NF, <span class=SpellE>Npresent</span>=
200, <span class=SpellE>tbn</span>=300, <span class=SpellE>Npass</span>=20000. The
dataset includes 45 autosomal microsatellite loci and 5 mitochondrial microsatellite
loci with 2 groups of mutation parameters. </span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>The headerRF.txt
file formalizes two scenarios: one with and one without bottleneck events.</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'><span lang=EN-US>TOY_EXAMPLE2_microsatellites_DNAsequence_two_pops_ancient_admixture<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>The
pseudo-observed dataset includes 2 populations with ancestral admixture between
2 unsampled pops at time ta=5000 (ra=0.5) that diverged at time t2=6000 with
N1=5000 and t1=1000 for 10 autosomal microsatellites 5 autosomal DNA sequences
and 5 mitochondrial DNA sequences with 3 groups of mutation parameters. </span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>The headerRF.txt
file formalizes two scenarios: one with and one without an ancestral admixture
event.</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'><span lang=EN-US>TOY_EXAMPLE3_SNP_INDSEQ_scenario3_MER_light_configuration<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>This toy example
is similar to the <span class=SpellE>IndSeq</span> SNP illustration of the
paper Collin et al. (2020) based on the pseudo-observed dataset generated from
scenario 3, except that only 100 SNP (instead of 5000) are requested for
simulation in the headerRF.txt file formalizing 6 scenarios to speed-up simulations.
</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>Warning: because
only 100 SNP are simulated, do not expect to obtain the same results as those
described in Collin et al. (2020).</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'><span lang=EN-US>TOY_EXAMPLE4_SNP_POOLSEQ_scenario3_MER_light_configuration<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>This toy example
is similar to the <span class=SpellE>PoolSeq</span> SNP illustration of the
paper Collin et al. (2020) based on the pseudo-observed dataset generated from
scenario 3, except that only 100 SNP (instead of 5000) are requested for
simulation in the headerRF.txt file formalizing 6 scenarios to speed-up
simulations.</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>Warning: because
only 100 SNP are simulated, do not expect to obtain the same results as those
described in Collin et al. (2020).</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:
normal'><span lang=EN-US>TOY_EXAMPLE5_SNP_INDSEQ_several_groups_of_loci_admixture<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>The <span
class=SpellE>IndSeq</span> SNP pseudo-observed dataset includes 3 populations
with pop 3 admixed between pops 1 and 2 at time ta=100 (r=0.4) and pops 1 and 2
diverging at time <span class=SpellE>ts</span>=10000 (N1=20000, N2=5000,
N3=10000, N4=10000). Note that NM=0.428571NF and MAF=Hudson. The dataset
includes SNP loci of different types: A=700 loci, X=100, Y=100 and M=100.</span></p>

<p class=Definition style='line-height:150%'><span lang=EN-US>The headerRF.txt
file formalizes three scenarios: one with and two without admixture event. The
headerRF.txt file requests only A=70 loci, X=10, Y=10 and M=10 to speed-up
simulations.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:24.0pt;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:
0cm;margin-left:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-pagination:widow-orphan lines-together;
page-break-after:avoid;mso-outline-level:1'><a name="_Toc62127992"><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:16.0pt;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-bidi-font-family:Calibri;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'>11. REFERENCES CITED</span></b></a><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:16.0pt;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-bidi-font-family:Calibri;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-bottom:0cm;margin-bottom:.0001pt;mso-pagination:
widow-orphan lines-together;page-break-after:avoid;mso-outline-level:1'><b><span
lang=EN-US style='font-size:16.0pt;mso-fareast-font-family:Calibri;mso-fareast-theme-font:
major-fareast;mso-bidi-font-family:Calibri;mso-bidi-theme-font:major-bidi;
color:#4F81BD;mso-themecolor:accent1'><o:p>&nbsp;</o:p></span></b></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:36.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-36.0pt'><span lang=EN-US>Collin

computation with supervised machine learning to infer demographic history from
genetic polymorphisms. </span><span class=SpellE><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:
normal'><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR'>Molecular</span></i></span><i
style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span style='mso-ansi-language:FR'> <span
class=SpellE>Ecology</span> <span class=SpellE>Resources</span></span></i><span
style='mso-ansi-language:FR'>. <span class=GramE>https://doi:</span>
10.22541/au.159480722.26357192<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:36.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-36.0pt'><span
style='mso-ansi-language:FR'>Cornuet J.M, <span class=SpellE>Ravign&eacute;</span>
V, Estoup A. 2010. </span><span lang=EN-US>Inference on population history and
model checking using DNA sequence and microsatellite data with the <span
class=SpellE>sofware</span> DIYABC (v1.0). <i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'>BMC
Bioinformatics</i> 11,401.</span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:0cm;margin-right:0cm;margin-bottom:0cm;
margin-left:36.0pt;margin-bottom:.0001pt;text-indent:-36.0pt'><span
class=SpellE><span lang=EN-US>Cornuet</span></span><span lang=EN-US> J.M., F.
Santos, M.A.&nbsp;Beaumont, C.P. Robert, J.M. Marin, D.J. Balding, T. <span
class=SpellE>Guillemaud</span>, Estoup A. 2008. <span class=SpellE>Infering</span>
population history with DIYABC: a user-friendly approach to Approximate
